Younger individuals with strong constitutions should use cooling agents; older individuals with weakened vitality should use warming agents.[6p]

病人因冒寒食冷而得者，宜辛温解之；因劳役冒暑而得者，宜辛凉解之。病人禀性怒急者，可辛凉解之；病人禀性和缓者，可辛温解之。病人两手脉浮大者，可辛凉解之；两手脉迟缓者，可辛温解之。如是之病，不可一概而用。偏热寒凉及与辛温，皆不知变通者。夫地有南北，时有寒暑，人有衰旺，脉有浮沉，剂有温凉，服有多少，不可差元。病人禁忌，不可不知。昔有人春月病瘟，三日之内，以驴车载百余里，比及下车，昏瞀不知人，数日而殂。又有人饮酒过伤，内外感邪，头痛身热，状如伤寒，三四日间，以马驮还家六七十里，到家百骨节皆痛，昏愦而死。此余亲睹。[7p]

If a patient falls ill from exposure to cold and eating raw food, they should be treated with warming spices; if they become ill from overwork in the heat, they should be treated with cooling spices. For patients with a hot and irritable temperament, cooling spices may be suitable; for those with a gentle and calm temperament, warming spices would be appropriate. If a patient has a large and floating pulse in both wrists, they can be treated with cooling spices; if the pulses are slow and weak, warming spices should be used. Such illnesses cannot be treated with a one-size-fits-all approach. One must be aware of the variations in heat, cold, and the use of warming or cooling remedies—they should not be applied rigidly. Just as the earth has its north and south directions, seasons have their cold and heat, individuals can be weak or strong, pulses can be floating or sinking, and the dosages of remedies should not be mistaken. Patients’ prohibitions and limitations must be understood. In the past, there was someone who fell ill during the spring season and contracted an epidemic; after traveling over a hundred miles in a donkey cart within three days, they became disoriented upon disembarking and died several days later. Another person consumed too much alcohol and suffered internal and external disturbances; they experienced headaches and fever that resembled typhoid. After being carried back home on a horse for sixty to seventy miles over three or four days, they arrived home in severe pain all over and died in confusion. I have witnessed these cases myself.[7p]

若此之类，不容更述。假如瘟病、伤寒、热病、中暑、冒风、伤酒，慎勿车载马驮，摇撼顿挫，大忌。夫动者火之化，静者水之化也。静为阴，动为阳。阳为热，阴为寒。病已内扰，又复外扰，是为重扰。奈人之神，讵能当之？故远行得疾者，宜舟泛床抬，无使外扰，故病不致增剧。又若伤寒时气瘟病，尝六七日之间不大便，心下坚硬，腹胁紧满，止可大小承气汤下之。[8p]

If it is of this sort, there is no need to elaborate further. In the case of plague, typhoid fever, febrile diseases, heatstroke, exposure to wind, or intoxication, one must be careful to avoid transportation by horse or carriage, which causes shaking and jostling—this is a major taboo. Motion is the transformation of fire, while stillness is the transformation of water. Stillness is yin, and motion is yang. Yang is heat, while yin is cold. When illness has already disrupted the internal balance, further external disturbances lead to aggravation, which is burdensome for the spirit—how can one endure that? Therefore, for those who fall ill on long journeys, it is advisable to float in a boat or lie on a bed, ensuring no external disturbances occur, so that the illness does not worsen. Additionally, if one experiences typhoid fever or plague and has not had a bowel movement for six or seven days, with hardness below the heart and tight fullness in the abdomen and sides, then one may administer a small dose of purgative decoction.[8p]

其肠胃积热，慎勿用巴豆、杏仁性热大毒之药，虽用一二丸下之，利五七行，必反损阴气，涸枯津液，燥热转增，发黄谵语，狂走斑毒，血泄闷乱，轻者为劳复，重者或至死，间有愈者幸矣，不可以为法。故伤寒新愈之人，慎勿食猪鱼杂果，酽酒湿面，及沐浴房室事。如犯，病必再发。爱其身者不可不慎。又如正二三月，人气在上，瘟疫大作，必先头痛或骨节疼，与伤寒、时气、冒暑、风湿及中酒之人，其状皆相类，慎勿便用巴豆大毒之药治之。元光春，京师翰林应泰李屏山得瘟疫证，头痛身热，口干，小便赤濇。渠素嗜饮，医者便与酒症丸，犯巴豆，利十余行。次日头痛诸病仍存，医者不识，复以辛温之剂解之，加之卧于暖炕，强食葱酢汤，图获一汗，岂知种种客热，迭发并作，目黄斑生，潮热血泄，大喘大满，后虽有承气下之者，已无及矣。[9p]

If the intestines and stomach are overheated, one must be careful not to use poisonous drugs like croton seeds or apricot kernels, as both are hot and very toxic. Even if one takes one or two pills, causing a laxative effect five or seven times, it will inevitably harm the yin energy, deplete the bodily fluids, and increase dryness and heat, leading to yellowing of the eyes, delirium, frantic movements, blood leakage, and disarray. In mild cases, it may lead to recovery from exhaustion, while in severe cases, it could be fatal, with only rare instances of recovery. Thus, one should not adopt this as a method.

Therefore, for those recently recovering from a cold, one must be careful not to eat pork, fish, mixed fruits, strong liquor, or engage in bathing or similar activities. If one violates this, the illness is sure to relapse. Those who care for their health must be vigilant.

Moreover, during the months of February and March, when the yang energy rises and epidemics are rampant, one will often first experience headaches or joint pains, resembling symptoms of cold, seasonal ailments, heatstroke, wind-damp conditions, or alcohol intoxication. One must be cautious not to use croton seeds, which are highly toxic, to treat such conditions.

In the spring of the first year of Yuan Guang, in the capital, a scholar named Li Pingshan contracted epidemic symptoms, including headache, fever, dry mouth, and dark, painful urination. He had a penchant for drinking, and the doctor mistakenly gave him a medicine meant for alcohol intoxication, which contained croton seeds, resulting in more than ten bowel movements. The next day, his headaches and other ailments persisted, yet the doctor was unaware and instead prescribed spicy warming remedies, and added that he should rest on a warm kang (bed stove), forcing him to consume scallion vinegar soup in hopes of inducing sweating. Unbeknownst to them, various heat-related conditions rapidly emerged together, leading to yellowing of the eyes, tidal fever, blood leakage, and severe shortness of breath. Although a purgative was later administered, it was already too late.[9p]

至今议者纷纷，终不知热药之过，往往独归罪于承气汤。用承气汤者，不知其病已危，犹复用药，学经不明故也。良可罪也。然议者不归罪于酒症丸者，亦可责也。夫瘟证在表不可下，况巴豆之丸乎？巴豆不已，况复发以辛温之剂乎？必有仲尼，方明公冶长之非罪。微生高之非直，终不肯以数年之功，苦读《内经》，但随众好恶为之毁誉，若此者皆妄议者也。不真知其理，遽加毁誉，君子之所不取。以予论之，凡伤寒之气有六禁：初病之时，甚似中酒伤食者，禁大下之，一禁也。当汗之时，宜详时之寒暑，用衾衣之厚薄，禁沐浴之火炕，重被热粥燔针，二禁也。[10p]

To this day, those who discuss it are numerous, yet they still do not recognize the fault of using hot medicine, often solely blaming Chengqi Decoction. Those who use Chengqi Decoction are unaware that the illness is already critical, and still administer the medication because they misunderstand the texts. This can indeed be blamed. However, it is also blameworthy that the critics do not hold the wine symptom pill accountable. When dealing with epidemic symptoms on the surface, one should not purgative, let alone use the pill made from cowbane. If cowbane is not effective, how can one continue to use the warming and acrid agent? There must be a reason why Confucius and the esteemed Gongye Chang are not at fault. The non-straightforwardness of Wei Shenggao is also questionable; he ultimately refuses to dedicate several years to the arduous study of the "Inner Canon," but instead follows the opinions and preferences of the crowd, thus earning both praise and criticism. Those like this are mere nonsensical critics. Failing to truly understand the principles, yet hastily attributing blame or praise, is not something a gentleman would do. In my opinion, there are six prohibitions regarding cold damage: at the onset of the illness, it resembles a case of food poisoning from drinking; thus, the first prohibition is against heavy purging. When sweating, one must carefully consider the current temperature and whether to use thick or light bedding, avoiding hot baths or heated kang beds, and being cautious with hot porridge and needles; this is the second prohibition.[10p]

当汗之时，宜详解脉之迟数用辛凉之剂，禁妄用热药，三禁也。当下之时，宜审详证下之药，禁巴豆、银粉丸方，四禁也。远来之病人，禁车载马驮，五禁也。大汗之后，禁杂食嗜欲，忧思作劳，六禁也。故凡有此者，宜清房凉榻，使不受客热之邪；明窗皓室，使易见斑出黄生之变。病者喜食凉则从其凉，喜食温则从其温。清之而勿扰，休之而勿劳。可辛温则辛温解之，可辛凉则辛凉解之。所察甚微，无拘彼此。欲水之人，慎勿禁水。但饮之后，频与按摩其腹，则心下自动。若按摩其中脘，久则必痛，病人获痛，复若有水结，则不敢按矣。正当禁而不禁者，轻则危，重则死。不当禁而禁者，亦然。[11p]

When sweating occurs, it is advisable to carefully examine the pulse for its slow rate and use cooling remedies, avoiding the reckless use of hot medicines—this is the first prohibition. At that moment, one should carefully consider the appropriate remedy, avoiding the use of Ba Dou (croton) and Silver Powder pills—this is the second prohibition. For patients who have come from afar, it is forbidden for them to be transported by cart or horse—this is the third prohibition. After significant sweating, one should avoid mixed foods and indulgent desires, as well as excessive worry and labor—this is the fourth prohibition. Therefore, for anyone with these issues, it is advisable to keep the room cool and the bed airy to prevent exposure to harmful heat; ensure the windows are bright and the room is well-lit, making it easy to observe changes in complexion. If the patient prefers cooling foods, then serve them cool; if they prefer warm foods, then serve them warm. Keep things clear without disturbance; allow them rest without exertion. If something can be treated with warming, use warming treatments; if cooling is needed, then apply cooling treatments. Observations must be very subtle without rigid restrictions. For those who desire water, be very cautious not to forbid it. However, after drinking, frequently massage their abdomen, which will help stimulate digestion. If one massages the middle area too long, pain will definitely occur, and if the patient experiences pain due to fluid accumulation, then they will hesitate to press on it. It is crucial to avoid what should be prohibited; if taken lightly, it may be dangerous, and in serious cases, it could lead to death. Likewise, if something is wrongly forbidden, the same applies.[11p]

　　　　丹溪心法 【元　朱震亨】

　　　　　瘟疫证治

　　瘟疫，众人一般病者，是又谓之天行时疫。治有三法，宜补宜散宜降。热甚者，加童便三酒锺。　　大头天行病，此为湿气在高巅之上，切勿用降药。　　冬温为病，非其时而有其气也。冬时严寒，君子当闭藏而反发泄于外，专用补药而带表药，如补中益气之类。
　　　　全生集 【明　陶华】

　　　　　大头伤风

　　大头者，一曰时毒，一曰疫毒。盖天行疫毒之气，人感之而为大头伤风也。若先发于鼻额红肿，以至面目盛肿不开，并额上面部焮赤而肿者，此属阳明也。或壮热气喘，口干舌燥，或咽喉肿痛不利，脉来数大者，普济消毒饮主之。内热甚者，通圣消毒饮。若发于耳之上下前后，并头角红肿者，此属少阳也。或肌热日晡潮热，往来寒热，口苦咽干，目疼胁满，宜小柴胡加天花粉、羌活、荆芥、连翘、芩、连主之。[12p]

Danxi Heart Method (Yuan - Zhu Zhenheng)

Epidemic Diagnosis and Treatment

Epidemics are illnesses that affect many people, also referred to as seasonal epidemics. There are three treatment principles: to tonify, to disperse, and to lower. For severe heat, add three cups of children's urine and wine. The "big head" epidemic is caused by dampness at high altitudes, so do not use methods to lower it. Winter warmth as a disease means the presence of its qi out of season. During the severe cold of winter, a noble person should close up and contain, and release it externally, mainly using tonic medicines along with exterior-releasing medicines, such as those that tonify the middle and boost qi.

Complete Collection (Ming - Tao Hua)

Big Head Cold

The "big head" refers to both seasonal poison and epidemic poison. It arises when the qi of the sky's epidemic poison affects people, leading to big head colds. If it begins with redness and swelling on the nose and forehead, resulting in a face that is highly swollen and unable to open, with red and swollen facial features, this is associated with the Yangming channel. If there is intense fever, shortness of breath, dry mouth, or swollen sore throat, and a rapid pulse, use the Pujixiaodu Decoction. If there is severe internal heat, use the Tongsheng Xiaodu Decoction. If it appears around the ears, both front and back, with redness and swelling of the head, this is associated with the Shaoyang channel. If there is daytime fevers, alternating chills and heat, bitter mouth, dry throat, eye pain, and fullness in the sides, use Lesser Chaihu Decoction with added Tianhuafen, Qianghuo, Jingjiao, Lianqiao, Qinqin, and Lian.[12p]

若发于项上，并脑后项下，及目后赤肿者，此属太阳也，宜荆防败毒散主之。若三阳俱受，邪并于头面耳目鼻者，以普济消毒饮，外用清凉救苦散敷之。大抵治法不宜太峻，峻攻则邪气不伏，而反攻内，必伤人也。且头面空虚之分，既着空处，则无所不至也。治法当先缓后急，则邪伏也。先缓者，宜退热消毒，虚人兼扶元气。胃气弱食少者，兼助胃气。候其大便热结，以大黄下之，拔其毒根。此先缓之法也。盖此毒，先肿鼻，次肿于耳，从耳至头，上络后脑，结块则止，不散必成脓也。[13p]

If it manifests at the back of the neck and under the base of the skull, as well as redness and swelling behind the eyes, this belongs to the Taiyang category; it should be treated with Jingfang Baidu San. If all three Yang channels are affected, and the evil manifests in the head, face, ears, eyes, and nose, administer Puji Xiaodu Yin and apply Qingliang Jiuku San externally. Generally, the treatment should not be too harsh; if you attack too strongly, the pathogenic qi will not submit and will instead retaliate internally, certainly harming the patient. Furthermore, if the head and face are depleted, this emptiness will reach everywhere. The treatment should start gentle and then become more intense, so that the evil can be subdued. The initial gentle approach should focus on reducing heat and dispelling toxins, while also supporting the vital energy of the deficient person. For those with weak stomach qi and poor appetite, aid the stomach qi as well. If their stools are hot and constipated, use Dahuang to purge and expel the root of the toxin. This is the initial gentle method. This toxin first causes swelling of the nose, then the ears, and spreads from the ears to the head, linking to the back of the brain; when it forms a lump, it will not disperse and will certainly turn into pus.[13p]

　　　　　时气

　　时气者，乃天时暴厉之气，流行人间，凡四时之令不正者，则有此气行也。若春应温而反寒，夏应热而反凉，秋应凉而反热，冬应寒而反温，此时行不正之气也。邪伤真气，若近秽气而伤真气，正如墙壁不固，贼乃敢入。若正气既盛，邪气难侵矣。其病势与伤寒相类。盖伤寒因寒而得之，时气乃感疫厉之气而得之，不可与伤寒同治，惟发散之药则同矣。凡发散汤剂，春感寒，邪在肝，升麻葛根汤。夏感凉，邪在心，调中汤。秋感热，邪在肺，苍朮白虎汤。冬感温，邪在肾，葳蕤汤。其瘟疫败毒散，若表不愈者，用羌活冲和汤、正气散、冲和羌活散、芎苏散，选而用之。[14p]

Seasonal Illness

Seasonal illness refers to the fierce influences of heavenly timing that flow through the human realm. Whenever the seasonal cycles are misaligned, this energy manifests. For example, if spring should be warm but instead is cold, if summer should be hot but instead is cool, if autumn should be cool but instead is hot, and if winter should be cold but instead is warm, then the air of improper timing is at play.

Such disruptive influences harm the true vital energy, akin to how a weak wall invites thieves. However, if true vitality is robust, it is difficult for evil forces to intrude. The ailments caused by this are similar to those of cold damage. Cold damage occurs due to cold weather, while seasonal illness arises from exposure to pestilential energies; thus, their treatments cannot be the same, although dispersing medicines can be common to both.

For all dispersing decoctions:

  • In spring, if there is cold, and the evil is in the liver, use Shengma and Gekegen decoction.
  • In summer, if there is coolness, and the evil is in the heart, use Tiaozhong decoction.
  • In autumn, if there is heat, and the evil is in the lungs, use Cangzhu and Baihu decoction.
  • In winter, if there is warmth, and the evil is in the kidneys, use Weirui decoction.

For pestilential disease and the dispelling of toxic energies, if the exterior does not recover, use Qianghuo Conghe decoction, Zhengqi powder, Conghe Qianghuo powder, or Xiong Su powder, selecting as needed.[14p]

　　　　　瘟疫

　　经曰：阳脉濡弱，阴脉弦紧，更遇瘟气，变为瘟疫也。此先因伤寒，前热未除，更感时行瘟气，而为瘟疫，治之当与瘟疟同也。
　　　　　寒疫

　　寒疫者，乃天之暴寒为病也。四时之中，天令忽有暴寒之作，若感冒即病者，名曰寒疫也，其证与正伤寒同，但暴寒为轻耳。若病初起，头疼发热，憎寒拘急，或吐逆恶心，中脘痞满，或饮食停留不化，或腹中作痛。未发热者，宜藿香正气散加减治之；若已发热者，十味芎苏散汗之；若身痛骨节疼发热者，羌活冲和汤加紫苏主之。若有汗，不可再发汗，宜加减冲和汤主之。若邪热不解，传入里变证者，宜从正伤寒条内治之。[15p]

Plague

The Classics say: When the yang channels are weak and the yin channels are tight, and when one encounters the plague qi, it transforms into a plague. This is often caused by an initial cold damage; if the prior heat has not been resolved and one is exposed to the seasonal plague qi, it results in the plague. For treatment, it should be approached similarly to that of the plague and intermittent fevers.

Cold Epidemic

The cold epidemic is an illness caused by severe cold from the heavens. During the four seasons, if the heavens suddenly bring about extreme cold, and it leads to illness similar to a cold, it is called a cold epidemic. The symptoms are similar to those of standard cold damage, but the severe cold is milder. If the illness begins with headache, fever, aversion to cold, and tightness, or with nausea and vomiting, fullness in the middle, or food stagnation and lack of digestion, or abdominal pain: if there is no fever yet, one should use a modified Huo Xiang Zheng Qi San for treatment; if fever has already developed, then a Xin Wei Qiong Su San should promote sweating. If there is body pain, joint pain, and fever, Qiang Huo Chong He Tang with Zi Su should be the treatment. If sweating has occurred, do not induce sweating again, but use a modified Chong He Tang instead. If the evil heat does not dissipate and transforms into internal symptoms, one should treat it according to the principles for standard cold damage.[15p]

　　　　医学入门 【明　李梴】

　　　　　疫疠

　　疫疾如有鬼疠相似，故曰疫疠，又曰时气。春应暖而反清，夏应热而反凉，秋应凉而反大热，冬应寒而反大温，非其时而有其气，凡感之者，即发头疼身痛寒热，一方长幼，病皆相似。治与伤寒微异者，春清责肝，升麻葛根汤；夏热责心，二香散调中汤；秋湿责肺，白虎加苍朮汤、茵陈五苓散；冬寒责肾，萎蕤汤、甘桔汤。土旺四季，随经取之。治与伤寒同者，表证败毒散，半表证小柴胡汤，里证大柴胡汤。挟内伤者，宜补宜散宜降，人中黄丸是也。经曰：疫气不拘于诊，更当于运气求之。[16p]

Introduction to Medicine
Epidemics

Epidemics are similar to ghostly afflictions, hence called epidemics, also referred to as seasonal illnesses. In spring, warmth should prevail but instead is clear; in summer, heat should dominate but instead is cool; in autumn, coolness should reign but instead there is great heat; in winter, cold is expected but instead there is excessive warmth. When these conditions arise out of season, those who are affected will show symptoms such as headaches, body aches, chills, and fever, regardless of age, all presenting similarly.

In cases that differ slightly from seasonal febrile illnesses: in spring, clear conditions involve the liver and are treated with Sheng Ma Ge Gen Decoction; in summer, heat involves the heart and is addressed with Er Xiang San or Tiao Zhong Decoction; in autumn, dampness affects the lungs and is treated with Bai Hu Decoction plus Cang Zhu Decoction or Yin Chen Wu Ling San; in winter, cold impacts the kidneys, treated with Wei Rui Decoction or Gan Ju Decoction.

When the earth is abundant across the four seasons, one should use remedies according to the classic texts. Treatments that are similar to those for febrile illnesses include Bai Du San for exterior syndromes, Xiao Chai Hu Tang for half-exterior cases, and Da Chai Hu Tang for interior conditions. For those suffering from internal injuries, the treatment should both replenish and disperse; Ren Zhong Huang Wan can be employed. The classics state: epidemic qi does not adhere to diagnosis, but rather should be understood through the nuances of seasonal changes.[16p]

凡入疫家用麻油服之，或纸捻蘸麻油，并雄黄朱砂末，探入耳鼻内，最能避秽毒之气，遍满乡村，兼用如意丹亦妙。　　经曰：春气温和，夏气暑热，秋气清凉，冬气冷冽。以伤寒为毒者，以其最成杀厉之气也。其有伤于四气，留在何经而发何病？大概春伤于风，夏必飧泄；夏伤于暑，秋必疟痢；秋伤于湿，冬必咳嗽；冬伤于寒，夏必痎疟。痎者，二日一发；疟者，一日一发。秋伤于湿病咳嗽者，及冬风寒相搏，痰涎生而为咳嗽。冬伤于寒病痎疟者，及春温气相搏，变为温病。是四时正气，亦能愆期而发，皆因发动之时，逆推致病之源。非受伤之时，预拟今日之病，故有久而消散不成病者，岂可执一论哉？但稍觉气淫于内，心腹不快者，不换金正气散加减以正胃气。[17p]

Whenever entering a house affected by an epidemic, use sesame oil, or dip paper wicks in sesame oil along with powdered arsenic yellow and cinnabar, and insert them into the ears and nose; this is the best method to ward off the foul and toxic air that fills the countryside. Additionally, using the Ruyi pill is also excellent.

The classics say: Spring brings warmth, summer brings heat, autumn brings coolness, and winter brings bitterness. The toxic effects of cold damage come from their capacity to kill. When one is harmed by the four seasons' qi, which meridian is affected, and what illness arises? Generally, if spring is harmed by wind, summer will certainly bring diarrhea; if summer is harmed by heat, autumn will surely bring fevers and dysentery; if autumn is harmed by dampness, winter will certainly bring coughs; if winter is harmed by cold, summer will certainly bring miasmic fever. Miasmic fever comes every other day; intermittent fever comes daily. Coughs resulting from autumn's dampness and winter's cold battling together produce phlegm and lead to coughing. If winter is harmed by cold, miasmic fever will arise, and with spring's warm air battling it, it will turn into a warm disease. Thus, the regular qi of the four seasons can also deviate in timing, all due to disturbances that push the source of illness backwards. It is not just the time of injury that forecasts today's illness; hence, there are times when lingering conditions dissipate without manifesting as illness. Should one simply adhere to one theory? However, if one feels some internal disturbance or discomfort in the heart and abdomen, do not change the formula of Jinxing Zhenqi powder; instead, adjust it to correct the stomach qi.[17p]

　　　　　寒疫

　　春分至秋分暴寒曰寒疫，非冬月伤寒比也。三月四月，或有暴寒，阳气尚弱，为寒所折，病热犹轻；五月六月，阳气已盛，为寒所折，病热则重；七月八月，阳气已衰，为寒所折，病热亦微。伤之者，其病与温暑相似而治则殊者，盖温暑伏寒自内而发，寒疫自外而入，宜调中汤为主，随时气候寒热轻重，而以辛凉辛温之药加减。盖折者，折抑阳气郁而为热也，感之轻而阳气不为所折，未至发热者，当于感冒药中求之。　　春三四月间暴热伤之者，亦名温病。伤寒汗下，过经不解者，亦名温病。但当随各经见证治之，皆不宜汗下。暴温，栀子升麻汤、九味羌活汤。过经和解，参胡芍药汤。[18p]

Cold Epidemic

When the spring equinox arrives and extends to the autumn equinox, a sudden cold is termed as a cold epidemic, which is different from winter's cold damage. In March and April, there may be sudden cold; the yang energy is still weak, so the cold can cause illness, but the heat symptoms are still mild. In May and June, as yang energy becomes strong, the impact of cold leads to more severe heat symptoms. In July and August, as yang energy wanes, the cold causes only mild illness.

Those affected will exhibit symptoms similar to summer heat but with different treatments. This is because summer heat arises internally with the cold, while cold epidemic comes from external exposure. A regulated middle decoction should be the main remedy, adjusted according to the varying temperatures and conditions. Spicy cool or warm herbs can be added or reduced accordingly. The weakening occurs when the yang energy is suppressed, leading to heat. If the symptoms are mild and the yang energy is not significantly affected and hasn't yet developed into fever, one should look for remedies within the cold prevention medicines.

In spring, if one is afflicted by sudden heat, it is also referred to as a warm disease. If the cold harm from sweating and purging does not resolve the symptoms, it is likewise termed as warm disease. However, one should treat according to the specific channel symptoms, generally avoiding sweating and purging. For sudden warmth, remedies like Gardenia and Schizonepeta Decoction or the Nine-Flavor Qianghuo Decoction are suggested. For those with unresolved symptoms, a combination of Ginseng, Peony, and other herbal decoctions may be recommended.[18p]

　　　　医贯 【明　赵献可】

　　　　　温病论

　　夫伤寒二字，盖冬时严寒而成杀厉之气，触冒之而即时病者，乃名伤寒。不即发者，寒毒藏于肌肤，至春变为温病，至夏变为暑病。暑病者，热极重于温也。既变为温，则不得复言其为寒，不恶寒而渴者是也。此仲景经文也。其麻黄、桂枝为即病之伤寒设，与温热何与？受病之源虽同，所发之时则异，仲景治之，当别有方，缘皆遗失而无征，是以各家议论纷纷，至今未明。刘守真谓欲用麻黄、桂枝，必加凉药于其中，以免发黄之病。张子和六神通解散，以石膏寒药中加麻黄、苍朮，皆非也。盖麻黄、桂枝辛热，乃冬月表散寒邪所宜之药，不宜用于春夏之时，陶氏欲以九味羌活汤，谓一方可代三方，亦非也。[19p]

On Febrile Diseases

The term "febrile disease" refers to illnesses caused by the severe cold and lethal energies of winter. When these energies come into contact with a person, they may immediately fall ill, and this is termed "febrile disease." If the illness does not manifest immediately, the cold toxin remains dormant in the skin and may transform into a febrile disease in spring or into a heat-related illness in summer. A heat-related illness is a more intense form of fever than a febrile disease. Once it has transformed into a febrile disease, it cannot be referred to as cold; those who do not despise cold yet experience thirst exemplify this. This is the essence of Zhang Zhongjing's teachings.

The herbs Ephedra and cinnamon twig are designated for the immediate illness of febrile diseases; what connection do they have with warmth and heat? Although the source of the illness is the same, the timing of the onset is different. Zhang Zhongjing treated these conditions with a distinct approach, which has been largely lost and remains unclear, leading to much debate among different schools of thought even today. Liu Shouzheng suggested that if one intends to use Ephedra and cinnamon twig, they must be combined with cooling herbs to prevent the onset of jaundice. Zhang Zihe's formula of Liu Shen Tong's dispersive powder, which incorporates gypsum, alongside Ephedra and Atractylodes, is also inappropriate. Ephedra and cinnamon twig are spicy and warm, and are suitable for dispersing cold pathogens in winter; they should not be used in spring or summer. Tao's notion that the Jiu Wei Qiang Huo Decoction could substitute for three different formulas is likewise incorrect.[19p]

羌活汤，易老所制之方，乃治感四时不正之气，如春宜温而反寒，夏宜热而反温，秋宜凉而反热，冬宜寒而反温，又有春夏秋三时为暴寒所折，虽有恶寒发热之证，不若冬时肃杀之气为甚，故不必麻黄、桂枝以散寒，惟宜辛凉之药，通内外而解之。况此方须按六经加减之法，不可全用也。不若逍遥散为尤妙，真可一方代三方也。然则欲治温病者将如何？余有一法，请申而明之。经曰：不恶寒而渴者是也。不恶寒则知其表无寒邪矣，曰渴则知肾水干枯矣。盖缘其人素有火者，冬时触冒寒气，虽伤而亦不甚，惟其有火在内，寒亦不能深入，所以不即发而寒气伏藏于肌肤，自冬至三四月，历时既久，火为寒郁于中亦久，将肾水熬煎枯竭。[20p]

Qianghuo Decoction, a formula created by Yi Lao, is designed to treat the inappropriate qi of the four seasons. For example, in spring it is suitable to be warm but instead it is cold; in summer it should be hot but instead it is warm; in autumn it should be cool but instead it is hot; in winter it should be cold but instead it is warm. Furthermore, during spring, summer, and autumn, there are instances of severe cold, which, although accompanied by symptoms of aversion to cold and fever, do not compare to the harshness of winter's sinister cold. Therefore, there is no need for Mahuang or Guizhi to disperse the cold; instead, it is better to use spicy and cool medicines to relieve both internal and external conditions. Moreover, this formula must be adjusted according to the principles of the six meridians and cannot be used in its entirety. It is better to use Xiaoyao Powder, which is particularly effective as one formula can replace three. If one wishes to treat warm diseases, what should be done? I have a method to explain. The classic states: if one does not dislike the cold and feels thirsty, this is the case. Not disliking the cold indicates that there is no cold evil on the surface; feeling thirsty suggests that the kidney's water is depleted. This is because such individuals have pre-existing fire; when exposed to cold qi in winter, though injured, it is not severe. The internal fire prevents the cold from penetrating deeply, which is why it does not produce immediate symptoms but instead hides beneath the skin. From winter into March or April, as time passes, the cold can stagnate within while the internal fire weakens, ultimately leading to the depletion of kidney water.[20p]

盖甲木阳木也，借癸水而生，肾水既枯，至此时强木旺，无以为发生滋润之本，故发热而渴，非有所感冒也。海藏谓新邪唤出旧邪，非也。若复有所感表，又当恶寒矣。予以六味地黄滋其水，以柴胡辛凉之药舒其木郁，随手而应，此方活人者多矣。予又因此而推广之。凡冬时伤寒者，亦是郁火证。若其人无火，则为直中矣。惟其有火，故由皮毛而肌肉，肌肉而腑脏。今人皆曰寒邪传里，寒变为热。既曰寒邪，何故入内而反为热？又何为而能变热耶？不知即是本身中之火，为寒所郁而不得泄，一步反归一步，日久则纯热而无寒矣。所以用三黄解毒，解其火也。[21p]

The wood element is associated with the spirit of yang, deriving its vitality from the water of the gui. When the kidney water becomes depleted, and at this time, the strong wood becomes vigorous without any source to nurture and moisten it, thus leading to heat and thirst, not due to an external cold invasion. Hai Zang states that new afflictions can provoke old ones, which is incorrect. If there is a new cold invasion, it will lead to aversion to cold. I use Liu Wei Di Huang to nourish the water, and Chai Hu, a cooling and acrid medicine, to relieve the stagnation of wood, responding flexibly to the body's needs; this method has brought many back to health. I also expand upon this principle. Generally, those who suffer from a cold during winter also exhibit symptoms of stagnant fire. If such a person has no fire, they are at the midpoint. Only when there is fire does it spread from skin and muscles to the internal organs. Nowadays, people say that cold pathogens penetrate inward, transforming into heat. If it is indeed a cold pathogen, why does it enter and then turn into heat? What causes it to transform into heat? It is unknown that it is the internal fire itself, trapped by cold, unable to vent, which then perpetuates itself. Over time, pure heat accumulates while cold dissipates. Therefore, I use San Huang to detoxify and resolve this fire.[21p]

升麻葛根即火郁发之也，三承气即土郁则夺之，小柴胡汤木郁达之也。此理甚简而易，只多了传经六经诸语，支离多歧。凡杂证有发热者，皆有头疼项强，目痛鼻干，胁痛口苦等证，何必拘为伤寒，局伤寒方以治之也。予于冬月正伤寒，独麻黄、桂枝二方作寒郁治，其余俱不恶寒者作郁火治，此不佞之创论也，闻之者孰不骇然吐舌。及阅虞天民《医学正传》伤寒篇云：有至人传曰，传经伤寒是郁病，余见之，不觉窃喜，以为先得我心之同然。及考之《内经》，帝曰人伤于寒而传为热何也？岐伯曰寒气外凝内郁之理，腠理坚致，元府闭密，则气不宣通，湿气内结，中外相薄，寒盛热生，故人伤于寒，转而为热，汗之则愈，则外凝内郁之理可知。观此而予以伤寒为郁火者，不为无据矣。[22p]

Shengma and Gegeng are treatments for fire constraint, while the three承气 (Chengqi) formulas address earth constraint. Xiao Chaihu Decoction resolves wood constraint. This principle is very simple and easy to understand, but it has been obscured by the various interpretations found in the classics, leading to confusion. All mixed symptoms that include fever typically present with headaches, stiff necks, eye pain, dry noses, rib pain, and bitter mouths. There is no need to restrict the treatment to just typhoid fever and its specific formulas. In winter, when typhoid fever is prevalent, I alone treat with Mahuang and Guizhi formulas for cold constraint, while for those who do not share a dislike for the cold, I treat with fire constraint. This is not a foolish invention, and those who hear it are often astonished. Additionally, when reading Yu Tianmin’s "Medical Correct Records" in the section on typhoid fever, it states that an enlightened person passed down that transmitted fever is a constraint disease. Upon seeing this, I felt secretly pleased, believing this echoed my own thoughts. On examining the "Inner Canon," the Emperor asks why people injured by cold manifest as heat. Qibo replies that the principle is that cold air condenses externally while causing internal constraint. The pores are tight and closed, so the qi cannot circulate freely, leading to the accumulation of dampness. Externally, cold pressure combined with internal constraint causes the heat to arise; thus, when a person is harmed by cold, it transitions into heat. If sweating occurs, recovery follows, which clarifies the principle of external condensation coupled with internal constraint. From this observation, it is clear that my view of typhoid fever as fire constraint is not without evidence.[22p]

　　　　景岳全书 【明　张介宾】

　　　　　论证

　　经曰：冬伤于寒，春必病温，是温病即伤寒也。然伤寒有四时之不同，如冬感寒邪而即病者，为真伤寒。其有寒毒内侵而未至即病者，必待春温气动，真阴外越，再触寒邪，其病则发。故至春犯寒则发为温病，至夏犯寒则发为热病，亦犹伤气者遇气则作，伤食者遇食则发，其义一也。然而伤寒瘟疫，多起于冬不藏精，及辛苦饥饿之人，盖冬不藏精则邪气乘虚易入，而饥饿劳倦之流则受伤尤甚，故大荒之后，必有大疫，正为此也。但此辈疫气既盛，势必传染，又必于体质虚浊者，先受其气，以渐遍传，则又有不待冬寒而病者矣。然此以冬寒主气之为病也。[23p]

Discussion on Diseases

The classics state: "In winter, one is harmed by the cold; in spring, one is sure to fall ill from warmth," indicating that warm disease is indeed a result of cold injury. However, cold injury manifests differently in each season. For instance, if one contracts a cold infection in winter, it is true cold injury. If cold toxins invade internally before manifesting as illness, they will wait for the warming influence of spring, at which point the genuine yang is overwhelmed and the cold pathogens reassert themselves, leading to illness. Therefore, if someone encounters cold in spring, it manifests as warm disease; if they encounter cold in summer, it appears as heat disease. This is similar to how those injured by qi flare up upon encountering qi, and those injured by food react to food—the principles are the same.

However, cold-related epidemics often arise when the essence is not stored in winter, particularly among the hungry and overworked. Not storing essence in winter allows the evil qi to invade easily, while those suffering from hunger and fatigue are particularly vulnerable. Thus, after a great famine, there will inevitably be a significant epidemic, precisely for this reason. Once this epidemic qi becomes prominent, it will surely spread, first affecting the physically weak and unclean, and then gradually spreading to others, leading to illnesses that do not necessarily wait for winter's cold. Nevertheless, these diseases are fundamentally attributed to the cold nature dominating the qi.[23p]

至于客气变迁，岁时不同，故有冬行春令则应冷反温，夏行冬令则应热反冷，春秋皆然，是则非其时而有其气，壮者无恙，怯者受伤，是又不止冬寒，而运气不正之害，所当察而慎避者有如此。　　瘟疫本即伤寒，无非外邪之病。但染时气而病无少长率相似者，是即瘟疫之谓。古人有云：瘟证因春时温气而发，乃因郁热自内而发于外，初非寒伤于表也，故宜用辛平之剂，治与正伤寒用麻黄者不同也。此说固若近理，而实有未必然者。盖瘟疫若非表证，则何以必汗而后解？故余于前论中，谓其先受寒邪，再触则发，诚理势之确然也。但其时有寒热，证有阴阳。治阳证热证者，即冬时亦可清解；治阴证寒证者，即春夏亦可温散。谓宜因证因时者则可，谓非寒伤于表也则不可。[24p]

As for the changes in weather and climate, they vary with the seasons. Hence, during winter, when following spring protocols, one feels cold instead of warmth; during summer, following winter protocols, one feels heat instead of cold. The same applies to spring and autumn. This results in a situation where there is the influence of the seasons without being in their proper time. The strong remain unharmed, while the timid suffer; this extends beyond just winter cold, reflecting the harm of improper climatic influences, which one should be aware of and carefully avoid.

Epidemics are essentially diseases caused by external evils, primarily manifested in the form of febrile illnesses such as typhus. However, when one contracts these seasonal conditions, the symptoms may not always align, leading to what we term an epidemic. The ancients have said that epidemic conditions arise due to warm air in the spring, which leads to internal heat manifesting outwardly, and not necessarily from cold injuries to the surface. Thus, it's appropriate to use mild, warming remedies; treatment differs from that for typical cold injuries with ephedra. This notion certainly has its basis, but it is not always true. If an epidemic were not a surface condition, why would sweating be necessary for relief? Therefore, in my earlier discussions, I posited that one first succumbs to cold influences, then manifests the illness—a logical conclusion. However, during that time, cold and heat can exist, and symptoms may indicate either yin or yang. Treatments for yang and heat conditions can indeed be effective in winter, while treatments for yin and cold conditions can be applied in spring and summer. It is advisable to tailor treatment according to symptoms and conditions; stating that superficial cold injuries do not occur would not hold true.[24p]

　　　　　脉候

　　凡病伤寒瘟疫，脉洪大滑数，而数中兼缓者可治。脉洪大而紧数甚者危。脉虽浮大而按之无力者，宜补兼表。身虽热而脉弱者，当以纯补为主，或微兼温散。身大热而脉见沉濇细小足冷者，难治。瘟病四五日，身热腹满而吐，脉来细而弦强者，十二日死。瘟病二三日，头痛腹满脉直而疾者，八日死。瘟病八九日，头身不痛，色不变而利不止，心下坚，脉不鼓，时或大者，十七日死。瘟病汗不出，或出不至下部者，死。瘟病下利腹中痛甚者，死。以上死证，言其略耳。诸所未尽，当于伤寒门参阅。[25p]

Pulse Diagnosis

In cases of illness from cold or epidemics, if the pulse is large, rapid, slippery, and also has a hint of weakness, it can be treated. If the pulse is large and rapid but excessively tense, it is critical. If the pulse is floating and large but lacks strength upon pressure, it is advisable to supplement and also address the exterior. If the body feels hot but the pulse is weak, the primary treatment should be plain supplementation, occasionally with slight warming dispersal. If the body is very hot and the pulse is deep, thick, fine, and the feet are cold, it is hard to treat. In cases of epidemic illness lasting four to five days, if there is fever, abdominal distention, and vomiting, with a pulse that is thin and string-like but strong, death occurs within twelve days. For epidemic illness lasting two to three days, with headache, abdominal distention, a straight and rapid pulse, death occurs within eight days. In cases of epidemic illness lasting eight to nine days, if there is no pain in the head or body, no change in color, but continuous diarrhea, with hardness under the heart and a pulse that is not bulging—sometimes strong—death occurs within seventeen days. If there is no sweating in epidemic illness, or if sweating does not reach the lower parts, death is imminent. In cases of epidemic illness with severe abdominal pain and diarrhea, death is expected. The above outlines conditions that lead to death, but other details should be referred to in the section on cold damage.[25p]

　　　　　治法六要

　　自古伤寒治法，苦于浩渺，余自考索以来，留心既久，每临编得其法，未必见其病，临病见其证，未必合其方。可见病多变态，执滞难行，惟贵圆通而知其要耳。故余注《类经》，所列伤寒治要有六，曰汗补温清吐下，然亦但言其概而未及其详。今悉诸法于此，用补伤寒之未备者。倘欲求仲景心法，仍当阅伤寒本门，使能彼此参证，则纲举目张，自有包罗贯串之妙，既约且尽，而活人之要，当无出此。[26p]

Six Essentials of Treatment

Since ancient times, the methods for treating cold-induced illnesses have been vast and profound. I have pondered this for a long time, and when I compiled these methods, I found that I did not always see the illness while encountering the symptoms, nor did I always match the methods to the conditions. This shows that diseases often change form and can be difficult to grasp. Therefore, it is essential to be flexible and understand the key principles.

Thus, in my commentary on the "Classified Classics," I have outlined six important principles for treating cold-related illnesses: sweating, supplementation, warming, clearing, vomiting, and purging. However, these merely present an overview without going into detail. I now summarize all the methods here to address what is lacking in treating cold illnesses. If one seeks the core principles of Zhongjing, they should still read the foundational texts on cold-induced illnesses, to be able to cross-reference and substantiate each other, leading to a comprehensive understanding. In this way, one finds precision and completeness, and the essentials for saving lives should not go beyond this.[26p]

　　　　　汗有六要五忌

　　治伤寒之法，余已析其六要，而六要之外，又有五忌者，何也？盖六法之中，惟汗为主，正以伤寒之愈，未有不从汗解者。故法虽有六，汗实统之，而汗外五法，亦无非取汗之法也。然取汗以辛散，此固其常也。而何以五法皆能取汗？六要则已，又何以有五忌之辩也？盖汗由液化，其出自阳，其源自阴。若肌肤闭密，营卫不行，非用辛散则元府不开而汗不出，此其一也。又若火邪内燔，血干液涸，非用清凉则阴气不滋而汗不出，此其二也。又若阴邪固闭，阳气不达，非用辛温则凝结不开而汗不出，此其三也。又若营卫不足，根本内亏，非用峻补则血气不充而汗不出，此其四也。又若邪在上焦，隔遮阳道，不施吐涌则清气不升而汗不出，此其五也。[27p]

Sweating has six essentials and five prohibitions.

In the treatment of febrile diseases, I have already analyzed the six essentials; beyond these six, there are also five prohibitions. Why is this? Among the six methods, sweating is the primary one, as recovery from febrile illnesses invariably occurs through sweating. Thus, although there are six methods, sweating truly encompasses them all, and the five methods beyond sweating largely also aim to induce sweating. Typically, sweating is achieved by using pungent dispersing ingredients. However, why can the five methods also induce sweating? If the six essentials are present, why is there a need for distinctions regarding the five prohibitions? The reason is that sweating results from the liquefaction of fluids, emerging from yang and originating from yin.

If the skin is tightly closed and the nutrients (ying) and protective (wei) energies do not move, then without using pungent dispersants, the foundational forces cannot open, and sweating will not occur—this is the first reason. Secondly, if pathogenic heat burns internally, causing the blood to dry and bodily fluids to deplete, then without using cooling methods, the yin energy cannot nourish, and sweating will not occur—this is the second reason. Thirdly, if yin pathogens are firmly closed, preventing the passage of yang energy, then without employing pungent warming methods, the flow will be blocked, and sweating will not occur—this is the third reason. Fourthly, if the nutrients and protective energies are deficient and there is an internal deficiency, then without using strong tonics, blood and qi cannot be replenished and sweating will not occur—this is the fourth reason. Lastly, if the pathogen is located in the upper burner, obstructing the pathways for yang, then without inducing vomiting or purging, the clear qi cannot rise, and sweating will not occur—this is the fifth reason.[27p]

又若邪入阳明，胃气壅塞，不以通下则浊气不解而汗不出，此其六也。凡此者，皆取汗之道，是即所谓六要也。何谓五忌？盖一曰热在表者，内非实火，大忌寒凉，寒则阴邪凝滞不散，邪必日深，阳必日败，而汗不得出者死。二曰元气本弱，正不胜邪者，大忌消耗，尤忌畏补，消耗则正气日消，不补则邪气日强，消者日消，甚者日甚，而必不能汗者死。三曰实邪内结，伏火内炎者，大忌温补，温则愈燥，补则愈坚，而汗不得出者死。四曰中虚气弱，并忌汗诸条者，大忌发散，散则气脱，气脱而汗不能出，气脱而汗不能收者死。五曰病非阳明实邪，并忌下诸条者，大忌通泻，泻则亡阴，阴虚则阳邪深陷，而汗不得出者死。是即所谓五忌也。能知六要而避五忌，伤寒治法，尽于是矣。但假热者多，真热者少，能察秋毫于疑似，非有过人之见者不能也。余之谆谆，其亦颙望于潜心者耳。[28p]

If a邪 has entered the Yangming and the stomach qi is obstructed, then without promoting a downward flow, the turbid qi will not disperse and sweat will not be released; this is the sixth point. All of these pertain to the method of inducing sweat, which is what is known as the six essentials. What are the five taboos? First, if heat is on the surface but is not true fire within, one must avoid cold; cold causes the yin邪 to congeal and not disperse, which will deepen the邪 and worsen the yang, resulting in death if sweating cannot occur. Second, if the original qi is weak and cannot overcome邪, one must avoid depleting; depletion reduces the正氣, and without replenishment the邪 will strengthen, worsening the condition until sweating cannot happen, leading to death. Third, if there is a real邪 inside that has formed and there is internal fire inflammation, one must avoid warm tonics; warmth further dries and tonics strengthen the邪, causing death if sweating cannot happen. Fourth, if the center is deficient and the qi is weak, all rules regarding sweating should be heeded; one must avoid dispersion; dispersing causes the qi to escape, and if qi escapes, sweating cannot occur, leading to death. Fifth, if the disease is not due to real邪 in the Yangming, one must avoid purging; purging depletes yin, and if yin is deficient, yang邪 becomes deeply entrenched, resulting in death if sweating cannot occur. These are the five taboos. To know the six essentials and avoid the five taboos is the entirety of treating febrile diseases. However, there are many instances of false heat and few of true heat; only those with exceptional insight can detect subtle differences. My earnestness is also aimed at those who delve deeply into these principles.[28p]

　　　　　汗散法

　　凡伤寒瘟疫，表证初感，速宜取汗，不可迟也。故仲景曰：凡发汗服汤药，其方虽言日三服，若病剧不解，当半日中尽三服。如服一剂，病证犹在，当复作本汤服之。至有不肯汗出者，服三剂乃解。若汗不能出者，死病也。此所谓汗不宜迟也。然取汗之法，又当察其元气病气之虚实。若忽尔暴病，表证已具而元气未亏者，但以辛平之剂直散之。若兼杂证，则当察其寒热温凉，酌宜而治，不得但知发散也。[29p]

Method of Inducing Sweating

In cases of cold and epidemic diseases, when the initial symptoms are present, it is crucial to induce sweating promptly; delay is not permissible. Therefore, Zhang Zhongjing said: In general, when inducing sweating through medicinal decoctions, even if the prescription states to take it three times a day, if the illness is severe and does not resolve, one should take all three doses within half a day. If after taking one dose the symptoms persist, one should take the original decoction again. If there are those who refuse to sweat, they may need to take three doses before relenting. If sweating cannot be induced, it is considered a deadly condition. This is what is meant by not delaying the act of sweating. However, when inducing sweating, one must also observe the balance of the vital energy and the pathological condition. If the disease arises suddenly, and the exterior symptoms are present without the vital energy being depleted, then one should simply use pungent and neutral substances to disperse the pathogens directly. If there are mixed symptoms, one should assess the nature of the cold or heat and treat accordingly, rather than merely focusing on dispersing.[29p]

又若身虽大热，表证全具，而脉见虚弱者，必不易汗。此即当详察补虚法酌而治之。若不知标本而概行强散，营竭则死。　　伤寒之宜平散者，以其但有外证，内无寒热，而且元气无亏也，宜以正柴胡饮为主治。此外如十神汤、参苏饮皆可酌用。若病在阳明者，宜升麻葛根汤。若感四时瘟疫而身痛发热及烟瘴之气者，宜败毒散，或荆防败毒散。若病在三阳而头痛鼻塞项强，身痛咳嗽者，宜神朮散。若伤风兼寒而发热咳嗽者，宜柴陈煎或金沸草散，甚者小青龙汤。[30p]

If the body is very hot, the external symptoms are all present, yet the pulse is weak, it is necessary to avoid sweating. One must carefully investigate and apply methods to replenish the deficiency. If the distinction between superficial and fundamental conditions is not understood and strong remedies are applied indiscriminately, it can lead to exhaustion and death.

In cases of febrile disease, where there are only external symptoms without internal cold or heat, and the vital energy is intact, it is appropriate to primarily use the formula "Zheng Chaihu Decoction." Additionally, formulas like "Shishen Decoction" and "Shensu Decoction" may also be considered.

If the disease is affecting the Yangming, one should use "Shengma Gegen Decoction." In cases of seasonal epidemics causing body aches and fever, or in the presence of miasma, "Baidu San" or "Jingfang Baidu San" should be used. If the disease affects the three Yang channels, leading to headaches, nasal congestion, stiff neck, body aches, and cough, "Shenzhusuan" is advisable. For cases of wind-cold with fever and cough, "Chai Chen Decoction" or "Jin Feicao San" may be indicated, and in severe cases, "Xiao Qinglong Decoction."[30p]

　　伤寒之宜温散者，以其寒邪外盛而内无热证，及元气无亏而气清受寒者，皆可从温直散之，宜二柴胡饮为最当。若寒甚表实者，惟麻桂饮为最妙，毋疑畏也。此外如五积散、麻黄汤、桂枝汤、小青龙汤、葛根汤、圣散子之类，皆可酌用。　　伤寒之宜凉散者，以其外热里亦热，必脉证俱阳而烦渴喜冷，及元气强实者，乃可兼凉兼散，宜一柴胡饮为先，或九味羌活汤、柴葛解肌汤，甚者六神通解散，皆可酌用。若内外俱热而或为热泻者，宜柴芩煎。若表里俱热而兼斑疹者，宜柴葛煎。　　伤寒之宜兼补兼散者，以营卫不足，血气不充也。[31p]

For those suffering from cold damage who should be treated with warming dispersions, this applies when the cold pathogen is predominant externally, and there is no internal heat, as well as when the original qi is intact and the qi is clear but affected by cold. In such cases, warming dispersions are appropriate, and the Er-Chai-Hu Decoction is the most suitable. If the cold is severe and the exterior is solid, the Ma-Gui Decoction is the most excellent choice, and there should be no doubt or fear. Additionally, formulas like Wu-Ji-San, Ma-Huang Decoction, Gui-Zhi Decoction, Xiao-Qing-Long Decoction, Ge-Gen Decoction, and Sheng-San-Zi can also be used as needed.

For those with cold damage who should be treated with cooling dispersions, this applies when there is external heat and internal heat, with a pulse presentation that is both vigorous and characterized by thirst and a preference for coolness, as well as when the original qi is strong and robust. In such cases, both cooling and dispersing approaches may be used, with the Er-Chai-Hu Decoction as the first choice, or alternatives like Jiu-Wei-Qiang-Huo Decoction, Chai-Ge-Jie-Ju Decoction, and in severe cases, Liu-Shen-Tong-Jie-San can also be used as needed. If there is heat both internally and externally leading to heat diarrhea, the Chai-Qin Decoction is recommended. If both the exterior and interior are hot and there are rashes, the Chai-Ge Decoction should be used.

For those with cold damage who require both nourishment and dispersion, this is due to insufficiency in the nutritive and protective qi and inadequate circulation of blood and qi.[31p]

用药如用兵，兵进而粮饷不继则兵复，攻病而元气不继则病复。故治虚邪之宜散者，必当先本后末，此其最要者也。若寒邪在营，肝脾血少，而邪热不退者，宜三柴胡饮或归柴饮。若寒邪在卫，脾肺气虚，而表邪不解者，宜四柴胡饮。若脾胃气血不足，而邪热不解者，宜五柴胡饮。若邪在半表半里，往来寒热，而微见气虚者，宜小柴胡汤。若温暑大热大渴，津枯液涸，阴虚不能作汗者，宜归葛饮。若寒邪深入，而阴中阳气不足，或背恶寒者，必难散解，非理阴煎不可。若中气大虚大寒，身热恶寒，或大便溏泄而表邪不能解者，非大温中饮不可。[32p]

Using medicine is like using troops; when the soldiers advance but the supplies are lacking, the troops will falter. Similarly, if we attack an illness but the vital energy is insufficient, the illness will relapse. Therefore, when treating the conditions caused by external pathogens, one must first address the root cause before the superficial symptoms; this is of utmost importance.

If the cold pathogen is within the nutritive level, with liver and spleen blood deficiency, and the pathogen's heat does not recede, one should use San Chai Hu Decoction or Gui Chai Decoction. If the cold pathogen is in the defensive level, with spleen and lung qi deficiency, and the exterior pathogen does not resolve, one should use Si Chai Hu Decoction. If there is insufficient spleen and stomach qi and blood, and the pathogen's heat does not resolve, one should use Wu Chai Hu Decoction. If the pathogenic influence is half-exterior and half-interior, with alternating cold and heat and slight qi deficiency, one should use Xiao Chai Hu Decoction. If there is extreme heat from warmth or summer, great thirst, with fluids depleted and unable to produce sweat due to yin deficiency, one should use Gui Ge Decoction. If the cold pathogen has penetrated deeply and the yang energy within the yin is insufficient, or there is severe cold in the back, it will be difficult to disperse; one must use a yin-cooking method. If there is great deficiency of central qi and extreme cold, with body heat and aversion to cold, or severe diarrhea with the exterior pathogen unresolved, one must use Da Wen Zhong Decoction.[32p]

　　　　　补虚法

　　伤寒瘟疫，俱外侮之证，惟内实者能拒之。即有所感，而邪不胜正，虽病无害。最畏者，惟内虚之人，正不胜邪，邪必乘虚深入，害莫大矣。故曰：伤寒偏死下虚人。且今人虚弱者多，强实者少，设遇挟虚伤寒，而不知速救根本，则百无一生。故伤寒书曰：阳证得阴脉者死，正以阴脉即虚证也。此欲辨之，惟脉为主，而参以形证，自无失矣。盖凡遇伤寒外热等证，而脉见微弱浮空，举按无力者，即是虚证，最不易解，最不宜攻。虽欲发汗，汗亦难出，即有微汗，亦不过强逼肤腠之汗，而必非营卫通达之所化。若不顾虚实而逼之太甚，则中气竭而危亡立至矣。然治虚之法，须察虚实之微甚。[33p]

Method for Supplementing Deficiency

Febrile diseases, like cold damage and epidemics, are both manifestations of external invasion; only those with internal excess can resist them. If one is affected but the evil cannot overcome the good, even in illness there’s no harm. The greatest fear lies with those who are internally deficient, for the good cannot withstand the evil, and the harmful influences will inevitably penetrate deeply, causing great damage. Thus it is said: "Cold damage primarily harms the internally deficient." Furthermore, many people today are weak and deficient, while those who are strong and robust are few. If one were to encounter cold damage with underlying deficiency and not know to urgently address the root cause, the chance of survival is nearly nonexistent. Therefore, texts on cold damage state: "Those with yang symptoms who have an阴脉 (yin pulse) will die," precisely because a yin pulse indicates deficiency. In distinguishing this, the pulse is primary, supplemented by physical signs, which ensures no error. Generally, when encountering cold damage or other heat-related symptoms, if the pulse appears weak, floating, and without strength upon pressure, this indicates deficiency; it is the most difficult to resolve and least appropriate to attack. Even if one wants to induce sweating, it is difficult for sweat to emerge. If some slight sweating occurs, it is merely forcing the skin to produce sweat, and it is certainly not something transformed through the nourishment of the ying and wei (nutritive and defensive) fluids. If one disregards the balance of deficiency and excess and pushes too hard, it will quickly exhaust the vital energy, leading to imminent danger. Thus, when treating deficiency, one must carefully observe the nuances of deficiency and excess.[33p]

若半虚者，必用补为主而兼散其邪；若太虚者，则全然不可治邪而单顾其本，顾本则专以保命，命得不死则元气必渐复，或于七日之后，或十四日，甚者二十日之后，元气一胜，邪将不攻自溃，大汗至而解矣。欲知其兆，亦察其脉，但得弱者渐强，小者渐大，弦者渐滑，紧者渐缓，则大汗将通，吉期近矣。凡用补之法，但当察其胸膈何如。若胸腹多滞者，未可补；年壮气实者，未可补。若气本不实，而胸腹无滞，则放胆用之。[34p]

If one is in a state of moderate deficiency, one must primarily focus on tonifying while also addressing the邪 (pathogenic factors). If one is in a state of severe deficiency, one should completely avoid treating the邪 and concentrate solely on restoring the fundamental essence. By focusing on the essence, one aims to preserve life; if life is sustained, the vital energy will gradually recover. It may take seven days, fourteen days, or even up to twenty days afterward for the vital energy to gain strength, and the邪 will naturally be defeated without any attack. When profuse sweating occurs, recovery will ensue. To understand the signs, one must also observe the pulse. If the weak becomes progressively stronger, the small becomes larger, the taut becomes smoother, and the tight becomes looser, then profuse sweating is imminent and a fortunate period is approaching. When employing tonification methods, one must observe the condition of the thorax and abdomen. If there is significant stagnation in the chest and abdomen, tonification should not be applied; if a person is young and has abundant energy, tonification should also be avoided. However, if the energy is inherently deficient and there is no stagnation in the chest and abdomen, one may boldly proceed with tonification.[34p]

又若内无热邪，而素宜用温，其或气有难行者，则必兼暖胃而后可。盖补得暖而愈行，邪得暖而速散，切不可杂用消耗寒凉，以分温补之力。其或初感寒邪，但见脉证真虚，邪不易散等证，则人参、熟地之类，开手便当速用，愈早愈妙。若或迟疑，则纵寇深入，反成难制，此治虚邪最善之法也。余用此法，活人多矣。尝闻昧者有伤寒忌补之说，不知补者所以补中，是即托里之意。亦以寒邪如盗，其来在外；元气如民，其守在中。足民正所以强中，强中正所以御外。保命元机，惟此一着，何为补住邪气？庸妄误人，莫此为甚。[35p]

If there is no internal heat pathogen, it is advisable to use warmth. If there is a difficulty in the flow of Qi, then one must warm the stomach before it can recover. For to补 (tonify) is to acquire warmth and promote flow, while the pathogen, when warmed, disperses rapidly. One must not mix with depleting cold or cooling methods, as this would divide the strength of warming and tonification. If one is initially affected by a cold pathogen and shows true deficiency in pulse and symptoms indicating the pathogen is hard to disperse, then herbs like ginseng and cooked rehmannia should be used promptly—the sooner, the better. Delaying will only allow the thief (the pathogen) to delve deeper, making it harder to control. This is the best method for treating deficiency pathogens. I have used this method to save many lives. I have heard that some ignorant individuals avoid tonics for fear of cold damage, not realizing that tonification is meant to support the interior, which is indeed a great principle. Just as a cold pathogen comes from the outside like a thief, the vital essence is like citizens guarding the interior. Strong citizens enable a strong interior, and a strong interior is what guards against the external. To preserve the essential mechanism of life, this is the only key to protecting against pathogenic Qi. To insist on avoiding tonification is to mislead people, and nothing could be worse than this.[35p]

余因再悉于此，用补伤寒治法之未备。渐用渐熟，方知其妙。自今而后，知必有不惑余言而受余之生者，将无穷矣。　　伤寒，精血素弱，或阴中阳气不足，脉细弱而恶寒者，必须大助真阴，则阳从阴出，而表邪自可速解，惟理阴煎加柴胡、麻黄之类，或随证加减用之为最妙。若伤寒于七八日之后，脉数无力，神昏气倦，或躁扰不宁，散之不可，清之不可，而邪不能解者，只宜理阴煎大剂与之，真回生神剂也。若气血俱虚，而邪不能解，只宜平补者，以五福饮为主，而随证加减用之。或大补元煎，或六物煎，或十全大补汤，皆可用。若脾胃中气虚弱，而邪不能解者，宜四君子汤加减用之。若中气虚弱，脾寒或兼呕恶而邪不解者，宜五君子煎、温胃饮。若劳倦伤脾，寒邪内陷，身热不退，当升散者，宜补中益气汤。若寒邪陷入，阴分血虚，不能外达，而当升散者，宜补阴益气煎。[36p]

I am therefore recounting this again here, as I have yet to fully grasp the methods for treating cold damage. Gradually using and becoming familiar with them, I am beginning to understand their subtleties. From now on, I know that there will be countless individuals who, without doubt, will accept my words and obtain life from me.

In cold damage, when the essence and blood are inherently weak, or when the yang energy within the yin is insufficient, the pulse is thin and weak, accompanied by a dislike of cold; one must greatly assist the true yin. Then, the yang will emerge from the yin, and the exterior pathogen can be rapidly resolved. It is best to prepare a formula that regulates the yin, adding ingredients like Chai Hu and Ma Huang, or adjusting according to the symptoms as needed.

If, after seven or eight days of cold damage, the pulse is rapid and weak, the spirit is cloudy, and there is fatigue, or restlessness and unease, if dispersing or clearing methods do not work and the pathogen cannot be resolved, then one should administer a large dose of a formula that regulates the yin, which is truly a revitalizing remedy.

If both qi and blood are deficient and the pathogen cannot be resolved, one should aim for a balanced tonification, primarily using the Five Blessings Drink, adjusting according to symptoms. Alternatively, one could use the Great Augmentation Decoction, Six Ingredients Decoction, or the Complete Great Tonifying Soup, all of which are permissible.

If the spleen and stomach qi is weak and the pathogen cannot be resolved, one should use a modified Si Jun Zi Decoction. If middle qi is weak, with cold in the spleen or accompanying nausea, and the pathogen cannot be resolved, one should consider the Five Jun Zi Decoction or Warm Stomach Drink. If fatigue damages the spleen, and cold pathogens invade, causing persistent fever, one should use the Middle-Boosting Qi Decoction. If cold pathogens penetrate deeply, leading to yin deficiency and blood weakness that cannot manifest outwardly, but when ascending and dispersing is necessary, one should use the Yin-Supplementing and Qi-Boosting Decoction.[36p]

若阴虚发热，面赤口渴烦躁，脉浮洪无力者，宜六味地黄汤大剂与之，一服可愈。凡中气虚寒表邪不解，或日久畏药，或诸药不效者，只宜独参汤，或浓或淡，或冷或热，随其所好，时时代茶与之，连日勿间，使其营气渐复，则邪气渐退，大有回生之妙，毋忽之也。　　伤寒用补之法，与用攻用散者不同，盖攻散所以去实邪，其力峻，其效速。故凡用柴胡、麻黄之类，取效在一二三剂之间；用大黄芒硝之类，取效在一剂之间。此而不效，必其用之不善，不可多也。至若用补者，所以补虚，其力柔，其功缓，虽于一二剂见效者，亦多有之。若积劳积损，气血虚甚者，欲其复元，诚不易也。但察其服补无碍，或于脉证间略见相投，便是得补之力。故轻者二三剂，重者十余剂，方得见功而汗出邪退以愈也。若不知此理，而但于一二剂间未见速效，则必致庸谗，起惑乱生而全功尽弃矣，此不可不深察也。[37p]

If there is yin deficiency with fever, a flushed face, thirst, restlessness, and a floating, rapid, and weak pulse, one should administer a large dose of Liu Wei Di Huang Tang, which can yield results after one dose. If there is a deficiency of central qi and the exterior pathogen does not resolve, or if one has developed a fear of medicine over time, or if various medicines have proven ineffective, then only Ren Shen Tang should be used. It may be thick or thin, hot or cold, according to the patient's preference, and it can be served as tea intermittently for consecutive days. This allows the nourishing qi to gradually recover, leading to the departure of pathogenic qi, resulting in significant restorative effects, which should not be overlooked.

The method of supplementation in treating cold damage differs from that of purging or dispersing. The purpose of purging and dispersing is to eliminate the substantial pathogen, demanding a forceful approach with swift effects; thus, when using herbs like Chai Hu or Ma Huang, results are expected within one to three doses, and with Da Huang or Mang Xiao, results can be seen after one dose. If there is no effect, it likely stems from improper use, and excessive application is unnecessary. In contrast, supplementation aims to restore deficiency, employing a gentler force with slower effects; thus, even if results are observed after one or two doses, it is common. However, if there is accumulated labor and severe deficiency of qi and blood, achieving restoration can be challenging.

One must observe whether taking supplements presents no issues, and if there is a slight correspondence between the pulse and symptoms, it indicates the power of supplementation is being obtained. For lighter cases, two to three doses may suffice, while for heavier cases, more than ten doses may be required to see results, leading to sweating and the retreat of pathogens for healing. If one does not understand this principle and expects immediate effects within one or two doses, it may lead to doubt and confusion, ultimately undermining the entire effort, which must be carefully considered.[37p]

　　　　　温补法

　　凡治伤寒瘟疫宜温补者，为其寒邪凝滞，阳不胜阴，非温不能行，非温不能复也。如寒气在经者，以邪在表也，宜用温散法，具如前。寒气在脏者，以阳气虚也，或宜温补，或止温中。然用温之法，但察其外虽热，而内无热者，便是假热，宜温不宜凉也。病虽热而元气虚者，亦是假热，宜温不宜凉也。真热者，谁不得而知之，惟假热为难辨耳。病假热者，非用甘温，热必不退。矧真寒者又在，不言可知。大都实证多真热，虚证多假热。故治实者多宜用凉，治虚者多宜用温。真假不识，误人不浅矣。又真寒假热之辨，则实亦有寒，实亦有热，虚亦有寒，虚亦有热。[38p]

Warming and Nourishing Method

In treating febrile diseases such as typhoid, those methods that warm and nourish are appropriate because the cold evil stagnates, and Yang cannot overcome Yin. Without warmth, movement is not possible; without warmth, recovery cannot occur. If cold qi is in the channels, the evil is on the surface and a warming and dispersing method should be used, as previously described. If cold qi is in the organs, it indicates a deficiency of Yang; in this case, warming and nourishing should be applied, or simply warming in moderation.

However, when using warming methods, one must observe if the exterior feels hot while the interior is actually not warm; this signifies false heat, indicating a preference for warming over cooling. Even if the illness presents with heat, if the vital energy is deficient, it is still false heat, and thus, warmth is favored over coolness. True heat is easily recognized, but false heat is difficult to distinguish. If one suffers from false heat, failing to use sweet warmth will result in persistent fever, especially when true cold is also present, which is evident without further explanation.

Generally, true conditions often show true heat, while deficient conditions usually present false heat. Therefore, true ailments tend to be treated with cooling methods, while deficient ailments are commonly treated with warmth. Misidentifying the true and false forms of heat can lead to significant mistakes. Additionally, distinguishing between true cold and false heat entails recognizing that both true and false can manifest in cold and heat states.[38p]

若谓实者皆热，虚者皆寒，则凿而谬矣。但实而寒者，只宜温散，不必滋补；虚而热者，只宜调补，最畏寒凉。盖寒凉无生意而善败元气，若以寒凉治虚证，则热未必退，且暂用则或可，久则无不败脾而危者。既已病热，又不宜寒，则总云假热，本非过也。　　伤寒发热而命门阳虚，或恶寒，或身痛，或呕或痢，脉弱气虚而表不能解者，必用大温中饮或理阴煎。若伤寒身热，心肺有寒，或呕哕而咳，或腹满而喘，止有寒邪而无虚者，宜小青龙汤。若阴证伤寒，自利脉沉身痛发热，腹痛厥逆，但有寒邪而元气无虚者，当用温药，宜四逆汤。若寒在太阴，腹痛吐利，或胀满厥逆，脾胃虚寒，而邪有不解者，宜温胃饮，或理中汤。[39p]

If one says that all that is real is hot and all that is empty is cold, then they are mistaken. However, things that are real and cold should only be warmed and scattered, not necessarily nourished; things that are empty and hot should only be regulated and replenished, and are most afraid of cold. Cold is lifeless and can easily damage the vital energy. If one treats empty conditions with cold, then heat may not necessarily subside, and although it may be bearable temporarily, in the long run, it will surely harm the spleen and lead to danger.

Having already suffered from heat, it is also inappropriate to use cold; thus, it can be generally stated that it is a false heat, which is not excessive. In cases of cold damage with fever and a deficiency of the kidney’s yang, or experiencing aversion to cold, body ache, vomiting, or dysentery, with a weak pulse and qi deficiency that cannot resolve the exterior, one must use great warming middle decoction or treat with yin regulating ingredients. If the cold damage presents with body heat and the heart and lungs are cold, or with cough and vomiting, or abdominal fullness with wheezing, where there is merely cold evil without deficiency, small Qinglong decoction should be used. If there is cold damage with yin symptoms, presenting with deep pulse, body aches, fever, abdominal pain, and reverse cold, but only cold evil without deficiency of vital energy, warming medicine should be used, preferably with the Si Ni decoction. If there is cold in the Taiyin and symptoms including abdominal pain with vomiting and diarrhea, or bloating and reverse cold, with spleen and stomach deficiency and unresolved evil, then warming stomach decoction or regulating middle decoction should be used.[39p]

若伤寒一二日，邪在太阳，或在少阴，背恶寒而表不解者，宜附子理阴煎，在仲景则用附子汤。若风寒在表，阴寒在里，外为身热，而内则泻利不能止，或见呕恶，或腹因利痛者，此其中气下泄，则外邪益陷，必不能解，宜速用胃关煎，或大温中饮。凡患伤寒有阴阳大虚，元气将败，而邪不能解者，非六味回阳饮不可。然但有大虚大寒之意，即当用此。若待其败，恐无及矣。[40p]

If typhoid lasts one or two days, with the pathogen in the Yangming or Shaoyin, accompanied by a severe cold in the back while the exterior remains unresolved, one should use the Fuzi Liyin decoction. In Zhang Zhongjing's case, he employed the Fuzi Decoction. If there is wind-cold on the surface, with internal cold causing heat in the body, while internals are experiencing persistent diarrhea, possibly accompanied by vomiting or abdominal pain, this indicates that the vital energy is leaking out and the external pathogen is deeply entrenched, resulting in an inability to resolve the condition. In such cases, one should promptly use the Weiguan Decoction or a Great Warming Decoction. In all cases of typhoid accompanying significant Yin and Yang deficiency, with the vital energy on the brink of collapse and the pathogen remaining unresolved, the Liu Wei Hui Yang Decoction is essential. However, if there is merely a sense of major deficiency and cold, one should administer this immediately; waiting until defeat occurs may lead to irreversible consequences.[40p]

凡阴盛隔阳，内真寒而外假热者，其证必头红面赤，或干渴舌焦，或口疮喉痛，或烦喘狂躁，或身热如火，或见虚斑而蚊迹遍身，或发阴黄而溺如金汁，虽其外有此证，而脉则微弱不鼓，且或为呕恶，或为泄泻，或背腹畏寒，或气短似喘，或昏睡无知，或惊惶惧怯，或虽热不渴，或言虽谵妄而气促声微，或身虽躁狂而举动无力，禁之则止，是皆内虚外实、真寒假热之证，须用理阴煎，或六味回阳饮、大温中饮、八味地黄汤之类，大剂与之，庶可保全。若虚火上浮，喉痛舌燥，不能热饮者，用井水浸药，冷与饮之，此用假寒之味，以解上焦之假热，真热之性，以救下焦之真寒，回阳起死，真神妙之法也。其有血气本虚，用补相便，然温补既多，而病日昏愦，且见烦热难愈者，此其阳邪独亢，阴气不至，而虚中有热也。但改滋阴，以犀角地黄汤加黄芩、麦冬，或一柴胡饮加知母之类。此十补一清之法，一剂即效，其妙如神。医中圆活，最宜知此。[41p]

When Yin is excessive and separates from Yang, resulting in true internal cold and false external heat, the symptoms will certainly be a red head and flushed face, possibly accompanied by dry thirst and a scorched tongue, mouth sores or throat pain, agitation and panting, body heat like fire, or the appearance of spots and mosquito bites all over the body, or the urine being yellow like gold. Although there are these external symptoms, the pulse will be weak and not strong, and there may be nausea and vomiting, diarrhea, a fear of cold in the back and abdomen, shortness of breath like panting, confusion and unconsciousness, anxiety and fear, or despite feeling hot there is no thirst, or even speaking in a delirious manner while breathing is shallow and faint, or the body may be agitated yet movements are weak; if controlled, they will stop. All of these are signs of internal deficiency with external excess, true cold and false heat, and treatment must include prescriptions to nourish Yin, such as the Six Flavor Rehmannia Decoction, Great Warming Middle Decoction, or Eight-Flavor Rehmannia Decoction, in large doses for preservation.

If there is floating fire, with throat pain and a dry tongue that can't tolerate hot drinks, use water from a well to soak the herbs, and drink it cold. This employs the flavor of false cold to resolve the false heat of the upper burner and the true heat to salvage the true cold of the lower burner, a method to revive the Yang and restore life, truly magical. For those with a deficiency of blood and the vital energy, use nourishing strategies. However, if warming tonics are administered in excess and the illness becomes increasingly confused, along with restlessness and heat that is difficult to relieve, it indicates that the Yang evil is solely excessive and the Yin energy is not adequate, thus there is heat within the deficiency.

In this case, modify to nourish Yin, using Rhinoceros Horn and Rehmannia Decoction combined with Scutellaria and Ophiopogon, or a Chai Hu Decoction with Anemarrhena, among similar formulations. This method of ten remedies to nourish and one to clear is effective with just one dose, its efficacy is truly miraculous. It is crucial for physicians to be agile and knowledgeable in this.[41p]

　　　　　清利法

　　凡治伤寒瘟疫，宜清利者，非止一端。盖火实者宜清火，气实者宜行气，食滞者宜消食，痰盛者宜化痰，皆所谓清利也。凡此数者，滞去则气行而表邪自解。然此宜用于邪实等证，而本非虚证之所宜。其有虚中挟实者，不妨少为兼用。此中权度，自有其宜。若病在危急，则毫不容谬。设不当清而妄用之，亦与扑残灯者无异也。　　伤寒火盛者，治宜清解。若热入阳明，烦渴躁热，脉洪便实而邪有不解者，宜柴胡白虎煎，或单用白虎汤、太清饮，或玉泉散；若汗后仍热者，亦宜用之。若伤寒口渴，烦热赤斑，脉洪大而无力者，宜人参白虎汤。[42p]

Principles of Purging

In treating epidemic fever, it is essential to clear and purify, which is not limited to just one approach. Generally, if there is excess heat, it is advisable to clear the heat; if there is excess qi, it is appropriate to move the qi; if there is food stagnation, it is necessary to resolve the food; if there is phlegm accumulation, it should be transformed. All of these methods fall under the category of clearing and purging. When these issues are resolved, the stagnation dissipates, allowing the qi to flow and the external evils to resolve themselves. However, these methods should be employed primarily for excess conditions and are not suitable for deficiency syndromes. In cases where there is a combination of deficiency with some excess, it is acceptable to use them sparingly. The key lies in discerning the appropriate measure. If the condition is critical, there should be no room for error. If one inappropriately uses clearing methods when they should not be applied, it is akin to striking a dying flame.

For cases of high fever in epidemic fever, the treatment should be to clear and resolve. When heat enters the Yangming stage, causing thirst, agitation, and a strong pulse with persistent evil, it is appropriate to use the Chai Hu Bai Hu Decoction, or simply Bai Hu Decoction, Tai Qing Drink, or Yu Quan Powder; if there is still heat after sweating, these remedies should also be used. If there is thirst, agitation, and red spots, with a strong yet weak pulse, Ren Shen Bai Hu Decoction is recommended.[42p]

若伤寒邪在太阳，发热头痛，脉洪大，表邪未解，而内热又甚者，宜一柴胡饮，或三黄石膏饮，或六神通解散。若六经通热，火邪不解，或狂斑烦躁，或头红面赤，口干舌黑，脉洪邪实者，宜抽薪饮，或黄连解毒汤，或加柴胡。若伤寒热入血室，吐衄斑黄，及血热血燥，不能作汗，而邪不解者，宜《局方》犀角地黄汤，热甚者宜《良方》犀角地黄汤。若热邪闭结血分，大便不通，而邪不能解者，宜《拔萃》犀角地黄汤。若少阴水亏，阳明火盛，热渴失血，牙痛便结，脉空作喘而邪不能解者，宜玉女煎。若伤寒阳邪亢盛，血脉不通，而四肢厥逆者，谓之热厥，宜四逆散。[43p]

If the cold pathogen is in the Taiyang (greater yang) stage, presenting with fever, headache, a surging pulse, and the exterior evil has not yet resolved, while internal heat is severe, one should use Chai Hu Decoction, or San Huang Shi Gao Decoction, or Liu Shen Tong Jie San. If the six channels are in a state of heat and the fire evil is unresolved, accompanied by manic rashes and restlessness, or a red face and dry mouth with a dark tongue, and a surging, static pulse, one should consider Chou Qin Decoction, or Huang Lian Jie Du Tang, or add Chai Hu. If the cold damage has penetrated into the blood chamber, resulting in vomiting, nosebleeds, yellow rashes, and blood heat and dryness, and the ability to sweat is lost while the evil persists, one should use the prescription of Xie Jiao Di Huang Decoction; if the heat is severe, use the Liang Fang Xie Jiao Di Huang Decoction. If heat evil obstructs the blood aspect, causing constipation and inability to resolve the evil, one should use the Ba Cui Xie Jiao Di Huang Decoction. If the Shaoyin water is depleted, Yangming fire is flourishing, leading to thirst, loss of blood, toothache, and constipation, with an empty pulse leading to wheezing while the evil cannot be resolved, one should use the Yu Nu Decoction. If the Yang evil of cold is excessive and the blood vessels are blocked, resulting in cold extremities, this is termed heat collapse; one should use Si Ni San.[43p]

若暑月时行瘟疫，表里俱热，宜清宜解者，羌活升麻汤。若伤寒热结膀胱，而小水不利，火邪不退，或挟热泄泻者，宜大分清饮，或柴芩煎，或益元散。若伤寒实热内畜，小水不利，而口渴烦热发黄者，宜茵陈饮，或大分清饮。凡瘟疫热甚而烦渴不宁者，宜雪梨浆时时与之，解渴退火最妙，大胜于益元散。至于冷水禀天一之性，甘而不苦，故大能清热解烦，滋阴壮水。凡火盛水涸，大渴便结，营卫热闭，不能作汗者，最宜用之。[44p]

If during the hot months a plague arises, and both inside and outside are hot, one should use Qianghuo Shengma Decoction to clear and resolve it. If there is a chill plague causing hot blockage in the bladder with difficulty urinating, and the fire pathogen does not recede, or if there is accompanying heat diarrhea, one should use Dafen Qingyin, or Chaiqing Decoction, or Yiyuan Powder. If there is a chill plague with strong internal heat, difficulty urinating, and thirst accompanied by heat and yellow color, one should use Yinchendrink, or Dafen Qingyin. In cases of intense plague heat where thirst is uneasy, it is best to provide snow pear juice at intervals, as it is excellent for quenching thirst and reducing heat, far superior to Yiyuan Powder. Regarding cold water, which has a natural characteristic of heavenly quality, being sweet and not bitter, it is particularly effective at clearing heat, alleviating restlessness, nourishing yin, and strengthening fluids. In instances of intense fire causing depletion of fluids, leading to great thirst and blockage of defense and nutrition, where sweating cannot be induced, this would be most suitable.[44p]

虽虚证不可用，然亦有当用者，但察其喉口热极，唇舌干焦，大便闭结不通，而大渴喜冷者，此阴虚水亏证也，不妨与人参、熟地、桂、附、干姜之属，相间并用，借以滋阴，其功不小。惟大便不结及微热微渴，劳倦阳虚等证，最不宜用。若妄用之，则多致寒颤而败。　　伤寒兼杂证者，治宜调和清利。凡伤寒兼风，发热咳嗽多痰者，宜柴陈煎。若食滞气实，邪结胃脘而表不解者，宜大和中饮加柴胡。若感四时寒湿之气，以致脾胃不和，或呕吐泄泻胀满者，宜平胃散。或寒盛多吐者，宜和胃饮。若外感风寒，内停饮食，头痛寒热，或为吐泻胀满者，宜藿香正气散。若感四时寒湿，发热发黄，身痛脉紧，中寒泄泻，小水不利者，宜柴苓饮。若中无寒而多火者，宜柴苓汤。若外伤暑热，霍乱泄泻，小水不利，腹痛胀满，内阴外阳者，宜五苓散。若外伤寒湿，一身尽痛者，羌活胜湿汤。[45p]

Although symptoms of deficiency are not to be used, there are still cases that warrant treatment. One should observe if the throat is extremely hot, the lips and tongue are dry and scorched, and there is constipation along with a great thirst for cold. This indicates a deficiency of yin and a loss of fluids. In such cases, it is appropriate to use ginseng, cooked rehmannia, cinnamon, aconite, and dried ginger in combination for nourishing yin, which can be quite effective. However, if there is no constipation and only mild heat and slight thirst due to fatigue or yang deficiency, these remedies should be avoided. Misuse can lead to chills and worsened condition.

For cases of cold damage with mixed symptoms, the treatment should focus on harmonizing and clearing. For cold damage accompanied by wind, with fever, cough, and excessive phlegm, Chai-Chen Decoction is advised. If stagnation in food causes an obstruction in the stomach while the exterior remains unresolved, Da-Hua-Zhong drink with Chaihu should be used. If one is affected by the cold dampness of the seasons, leading to disharmony in the spleen and stomach, or symptoms such as vomiting, diarrhea, and bloating, Pingwei Powder is appropriate. If there is significant cold causing frequent vomiting, Hewei Drink is recommended. If externally contracted wind-cold leads to internal stagnation of food, accompanied by headaches, alternating chills and fever, or symptoms like vomiting, diarrhea, and bloating, Huo-Xiang Zheng-Qi Powder should be administered.

For cases of seasonal cold dampness with fever, jaundice, body aches, and tight pulse, along with cold diarrhea and difficulty urinating, Chai-Ling Decoction is suitable. If there is a lack of cold but an abundance of fire internally, Chai-Ling Soup is indicated. For cases of heat from external injury causing cholera-like diarrhea, difficulty urinating, abdominal pain, and bloating with internal yin and exterior yang conditions, Wu-Ling Powder is the remedy. For external injury from cold and dampness resulting in pain throughout the body, Qianghuo Shengshi Decoction should be used.[45p]

　　　　　吐法

　　凡伤寒宜吐者，必其上焦有滞，或食或痰，结聚胸膈，而邪不得散者，当吐也。或寒邪浊气内陷膈间，而为痞为痛者，当吐也。盖吐中自有发散之意。若中气虚寒，脉弱无力，及气短虚烦不宁者，皆不可吐。凡用吐药，中病即止，不必尽剂。　　古方吐法，多用独圣散及茶调散。凡上焦邪滞，皆可用之。然不若新吐法为更捷也。又凡诸药皆可吐，只随证用药煎汤，服少顷，揉而吐之，则轻重可酌，标本可兼，尤其善也。[46p]

Vomiting Therapy

For cases of febrile diseases where vomiting is advisable, it is essential that there is stagnation in the upper jiao, whether caused by food or phlegm, leading to a blockage in the chest and diaphragm, preventing the邪 (evil) from dispersing; in such cases, vomiting should be performed. If there is cold邪 and turbid qi penetrating into the diaphragm, resulting in distension or pain, vomiting should also be done. The act of vomiting inherently expresses a principle of dispersing. However, if there is a deficiency of middle qi with cold, a weak and powerless pulse, or symptoms of shortness of breath accompanied by restlessness, then vomiting must not be performed.

When using emetic medicines, one should stop at the moment the illness begins to improve; it is not necessary to expel everything. Ancient methods of emesis predominantly utilized the Dusheng Powder and tea adjustments. Any stagnation in the upper jiao can be treated with these. However, the new methods of vomiting are regarded as more efficient. Additionally, all medicines can be used for vomiting; one merely needs to prepare the medicinal decoction according to the symptoms, take it for a short while, then knead and vomit, allowing for a tailored approach based on severity and symptomatology, which is particularly effective.[46p]

　　　　　下法

　　凡伤寒瘟疫宜下者，必阳明邪实于腑，而秘结腹满者，乃可下之。或元气素强，胃气素实者，亦可下之。若大便虽数日不行，而腹无胀满，及大便无壅滞不通之状，或连日不食，而脐腹坦然，软而无碍者，此其阳明胃腑，本无实邪，切不可妄下妄导，以泄中气。又如伤寒门忌下诸条，必当加意详察，不可误用。盖诸误之害，下为尤甚，不可忽也。今见时医有妄下而亦不致死者，必其元气之素强，能胜攻下者也。若概引为证，必致杀人。[47p]

Alternatives for Treatment of Febrile Diseases

In cases of cold damage or epidemics where purging is indicated, it is essential that there is an obstruction in the Yangming channel due to excess in the bowels, leading to secreted accumulation and abdominal fullness, before initiating purgation. If the patient has inherently strong vital energy and a robust stomach, purging can also be considered. However, if there has been no bowel movement for several days, yet the abdomen is not distended, and there are no signs of constipation or blockage, and if the patient has not eaten for consecutive days but the abdomen remains relaxed and unobstructed, it indicates that the Yangming stomach and bowels are not truly obstructed by excess, and care must be taken to avoid reckless purging that could deplete the interior energy. Furthermore, the rules against purging in cases of cold damage should be heeded carefully, so as not to misapply treatment. Misjudgments in this regard can have particularly severe consequences. Although there may be instances where some physicians recklessly administer purgatives without causing death, it is likely because the patient’s vital energy is naturally strong enough to withstand the effects of purging. Relying on such examples as justification could result in fatal outcomes.[47p]

　　伤寒邪入阳明，便秘谵语，腹满烦热，脉证俱实者，宜大承气汤，或调胃承气汤。若伤寒表证未除，里证又急，表里俱实者，宜大柴胡汤。若三焦六经邪火壅结，大便不通，而表邪不解者，宜《局方》凉膈散。若伤寒热邪传里，当下而气血俱虚者，宜陶氏黄龙汤。若伤寒热邪传里，而血虚闭结，腹胀作痛，邪不能解者，宜五烛散。若时气瘟疫遍行，火邪内蓄，三焦实热，大便秘结，而邪不能退者，宜五瘟丹。若时行瘟疫发热，火浮于上，胸膈结热者，宜大清丸。凡诸有宜通宜下者，但随证作引，送百顺丸一二三钱，最捷最妙。[48p]

If the cold evil enters the Yangming and there are symptoms of constipation, delirium, fullness in the abdomen, and a firm pulse, then it is advisable to use Da Cheng Qi Decoction or adjust it with Tiao Wei Cheng Qi Decoction. If the exterior symptoms of the cold have not been resolved but there is an urgency in the interior, and both the exterior and interior are firm, Da Chai Hu Decoction should be used. If there is a blockage of heat evil in the three jiaos and six meridians, with constipation and unresolved exterior symptoms, then the prescribed Liang Ge San should be administered. If the cold and heat evil has penetrated the interior leading to deficiency of both qi and blood, then Tao's Huang Long Decoction is appropriate. If the heat evil has penetrated the interior while there is blood deficiency causing blockage with abdominal distention and pain, and the evil cannot be resolved, then Wu Zhu San should be used. If there is a widespread epidemic causing heat with internal fire accumulation in the three jiaos, resulting in constipation and the evil cannot be dispelled, then Wu Wen Dan is recommended. If there is an epidemic causing fever, with floating heat on the surface and heat accumulation in the chest, Da Qing Wan should be used. For all conditions that require purging or laxation, one should follow the symptoms and administer Bai Shun Wan in quantities of one, two, or three qian, as it is the most swift and excellent remedy.[48p]

　　　　　瘟疫热毒辨治

　　瘟疫本即伤寒，然亦有稍异。以其多发于春夏，且因时气遍行，大小相似，必待日数足，然后得汗而解者，是为瘟疫之证。虽古法云瘟病在三阳者多，三阴者少，然亦不可拘泥。若见阴证阴脉，是即三阴病也，大宜辨而治之。　　瘟疫之在三阳者，当辨其经。如脉浮头疼，发热身痛者，太阳证也，宜九味羌活汤加减治之。若脉长鼻干，不眠而躁者，阳明病也，宜葛根解肌汤，或十味参苏饮加减治之。若脉弦而数，胸胁痛而耳聋，少阳证也，宜小柴胡汤加减治之。按此三阳之治，乃古方治瘟之大略。[49p]

Differentiation and Treatment of Epidemic Heat Toxins

Epidemics fundamentally correspond to typhoid fever, but they can have slight differences. They often occur in spring and summer, and due to the prevailing climate, they manifest similarly in severity. One must wait until the disease has run its course before sweating can alleviate it; this is the hallmark of an epidemic. Although ancient methods state that epidemic illnesses are more prevalent in the three yang channels and less so in the three yin, one should not be overly rigid in this classification. If one observes symptoms of yin and the pulse is yin, this indicates a three yin disease and should be clearly differentiated and treated.

For epidemics in the three yang channels, one must discern their respective pathways. If the pulse is floating, with a headache, fever, and body aches, this is a Taiyang syndrome; treat it with a modified version of the Nine-Flavor Qianghuo Decoction.
