If the pulse is long, the nose is dry, and there is insomnia with restlessness, this indicates a Yangming syndrome; treat it with Ge Gen Jie Mu Decoction or a modified version of the Ten-Flavor Ren Su Decoction. If the pulse is wiry and rapid, accompanied by chest and flank pain and deafness, this is a Shaoyang syndrome; treat it with a modified version of Xiao Chai Hu Decoction. This approach to treating the three yang channels is a key aspect of ancient methods for addressing epidemics.[49p]

然此证寒热虚实，无所不有，仍当察治如前，不可拘也。　　瘟疫初起而头疼身痛，憎寒发热，脉紧数洪滑，而别无他证，先宜正柴胡饮，或败毒散，或十神汤。若瘟疫初起，多阴少阳，脉证无虚者，宜神朮散。若瘟疫胸膈满闷，小柴胡加枳实、橘红；热在内者，仍加黄连。若暑月时行瘟疫，表里俱热甚，宜清火解毒者，羌活升麻汤。若瘟疫火盛，脉洪大而热躁甚者，三黄石膏汤。若瘟疫热毒上浮，头面俱肿，目不能开，口干舌燥，咽喉不利者，普济消毒饮。若瘟疫脉洪大，烦躁热渴者，白虎汤；或兼呕吐者，仲景竹叶石膏汤。[50p]

However, this evidence of cold, heat, deficiency, and excess is all-encompassing, and it should still be treated as before, without being rigidly adhered to. When an epidemic first arises with symptoms of headache and body aches, aversion to cold and fever, a tight and rapid pulse, and no other symptoms, it is advisable to use Chai Hu Decoction, or Bai Du San, or Shi Shen Tang. If the epidemic begins with more yin and less yang, and the pulse shows no deficiency, Shen Zhu San should be used. If there is fullness and oppression in the chest due to the epidemic, Xiao Chai Hu Tang should be modified with Zhi Shi and Ju Hong; if there is internal heat, add Huang Lian. In hot months when epidemics occur, with both exterior and interior heat being severe, it is appropriate to use Qiang Huo Sheng Ma Decoction to clear heat and resolve toxins. If the epidemic exhibits strong fire symptoms, with a large and rapid pulse and severe agitation, San Huang Shi Gao Tang should be used. If the heat and toxins from the epidemic rise, causing swelling in the head and face, inability to open the eyes, dryness of the mouth and tongue, and difficulty swallowing, Pu Ji Xiao Du Yin is recommended. If the epidemic presents with a large and rapid pulse, causing agitation and thirst, Bai Hu Tang is suitable; or if there are accompanying symptoms of vomiting, use Zhong Jing Zhu Ye Shi Gao Tang.[50p]

若瘟疫发狂谵语，脉洪大滑实，而大便秘结不通者，大承气汤，或鸡子清饮。若瘟疫内外俱有实邪，大便不通，当表里双解者，防风通圣散。若瘟疫病八九日不退，而发斑发黄，但脉不虚不浮紧，而腹见痞满者，率可以承气、五苓合服而下之。若瘟疫头身红赤，肢体热甚，烦躁不能当者，宜用解瘟疫热毒法，及内饮雪梨浆，或用井华水调玉泉散，俱妙。按以上诸法，乃因时因证，皆阳证实邪之所宜。[51p]

If the plague causes rampant delirium, with a pulse that is surging, large, and slippery, and if there is constipation, one should use the Da Cheng Qi Decoction or the Jizi Qing Drink. If the plague has both internal and external solid pathogens and there is constipation, one should use the Fang Feng Tong Sheng San to resolve conditions both inside and out. If the plague lingers for eight to nine days without resolving, with rashes and yellowing in the skin, but the pulse is neither weak nor floating and the abdomen feels distended, one should generally combine the Da Cheng Qi Decoction and the Wu Ling San to promote a bowel movement. If the plague presents with redness in the head and body, extreme heat in the limbs, and restlessness that is unbearable, one should use methods to resolve the plague's heat toxins, drink inner snow pear juice, or mix Jinghua water with Yuquan Powder, all of which are excellent. The above methods are tailored to the situation and symptoms, suitable for Yang patterns with solid pathogens.[51p]

若瘟疫脉弱无力，或外虽实而内则虚，或口不喜冷，大便不结之类，即非阳证，不得以身热脉数，俱认为火，虽在暑月，如理中汤、理阴煎、大温中饮、大补元煎及前温补诸法，皆当随证必用，此舍时从证之妙法也。矧夏月尤多伏阴，故凡临此证者，必先察阴阳，次辨虚实，则其要也。宜切识之！　　徐东皋曰：瘟疫六七日不解，以至热入血室发黄，身如烟熏，目如金色，口燥而热结，以砭针刺曲池出恶血，仍以通圣散兼散兼下，得汗如黄水，粪如黑膏而即愈。按此即北方之所谓打寒也。其法用手捋上膊，使血聚于臂，以帛缚定，乃用箸夹磁锋，击刺肘中曲泽旁之大络，使邪毒随恶血而出，亦最捷之法。穷人用之极效，然非曲池穴也。[52p]

If the epidemic shows weak and powerless pulses, or appears solid externally but is empty internally, or if one dislikes cold drinks and experiences loose stools, it is not a yang condition. One must not hastily conclude it is fire due to fever and rapid pulse, even in the summer months. Treatments such as Li Zhong Tang, Li Yin Jian, Da Wen Zhong Yin, Da Bu Yuan Jian, and other warming methods should be applied according to the specific symptoms; this is the subtle method of adapting treatment to the condition rather than the time. Furthermore, summer months are particularly rife with hidden yin, so for every case of this nature, one must first assess yin and yang, and then distinguish between deficiency and fullness; this is essential. It is crucial to recognize this!

Xu Donggao said: If the epidemic does not resolve after six or seven days, and heat enters the blood chamber causing yellowing, the body feels as if it has been smoked, the eyes appear golden, the mouth is dry and hot with hardened stools, then one should use a needle to prick the cubital region to expel bad blood, along with using Tong Sheng San combined with a purgative, achieving sweating like yellow water and stools like black grease for recovery. This is what is referred to in the North as "striking the cold." The method involves using the hand to stroke the upper arm to gather blood to the arm, securing it with a cloth, then using chopsticks to pinch the magnetic ridge, striking and pricking the large collaterals beside the elbow's curve, allowing the pathogenic toxins to exit alongside the bad blood; this is also the most effective method. The impoverished have found it highly effective, yet it is not specifically at the point of Qu Chi.[52p]

　　　　　大头瘟证治

　　大头瘟者，以天行邪毒，客于三阳之经，所以憎寒发热，头目颈项，或咽喉俱肿，甚至腮面红赤，肩背斑肿，状如虾蟆，故又名为虾蟆瘟。大都此证多属风热，然亦有表里虚实之辨。又外科有时毒证，亦即此也。　　一大头虾蟆瘟治法。凡病在头目，内火未盛者，先当解散，宜正柴胡饮或败毒散。若时毒咽喉肿痛，内火不甚，而便利调和者，葛根牛蒡汤。时毒表里俱热，头目俱肿，宜清宜散者，柴葛煎。若毒在阳明，表里俱热，多头痛鼻干，宜散者，柴葛解肌汤。若时毒三阳热极狂躁，咽喉肿痛，宜清兼散者，栀子仁汤。[53p]

Treatment for Big Head Pestilence

The Big Head Pestilence is caused by the malevolent toxins of heaven affecting the channels of the three Yangs, resulting in a hatred of cold, fever, swelling of the head, neck, or throat, and even redness of the cheeks and face, with swelling of the shoulders and back, resembling a toad; hence it is also known as Toad Pestilence. Generally, this condition is mostly due to wind-heat, but there can be distinctions between superficial and internal deficiencies or excesses. There are also times when external toxic conditions manifest as this.

Treatment methods for Big Head Toad Pestilence:

  1. When the illness is localized in the head and internal heat is not excessive, the first approach should be to disperse it, using Chai Hu decoction or Bai Du San.
  2. If the throat is swollen and painful due to the current toxin, with moderate internal heat and smooth adjustments, Ge Gen Niu Bang Tang is appropriate.
  3. When the external and internal heat are both present, with swelling in the head and neck, and clearance along with dispersion is needed, use Chai Ge Decoction.
  4. If the current toxin in the Yangming is causing both external and internal heat with severe headaches and nasal dryness, a dispersing approach is suitable with Chai Ge Jie Ji Tang.
  5. If the current toxin in the three Yangs is extremely hot and tumultuous, with swollen and painful throat, a combined approach of clearing and dispersing is recommended with Zhi Zi Ren Tang.[53p]

若时毒遍行，邪热上浮，头面俱肿，咽喉不利者，普济消毒饮。若时毒风热上聚头面，宜升散者，犀角升麻汤。若时气盛行宜清火解毒者，羌活升麻汤。若时毒血热烦躁兼赤斑者，犀角散、人参白虎汤。若时毒内外俱实，当双解者，防风通圣散。若时毒焮肿作痛，脉实便秘，宜下者，五利大黄汤，或漏芦升麻汤，或连翘消毒散。若时毒虽盛而外实内虚，脉弱神困，凡诸虚证有据者，必当救里内托，宜参芪托里散，或托里消毒散。其有阳虚假热，而兼呕恶泄泻者，如六味回阳饮之类，皆所必用，不可疑也。若头项肿甚疼痛难忍者，宜用清凉救苦散敷之，或取侧柏叶自然汁调蚯蚓泥敷之。[54p]

If there is widespread toxicity causing邪热 to rise, resulting in swelling of the head and face and difficulty in the throat, the remedy is Puji Xiaodu Decoction. If the毒风热 gathers in the head and face, leading to elevation and dispersal issues, Rhinoceros Horn and Cimicifuga Decoction is recommended. If there is a prevailing气 that requires clearing heat and resolving toxicity, Qianghuo and Cimicifuga Decoction should be used. If there are symptoms of toxic blood heat, agitation, and red patches, you may use Rhinoceros Horn Powder or Ginseng and Baihu Decoction. If both internal and external toxicity are strong and a dual resolution is required, Fangfeng Tongsheng Powder is appropriate. If the toxicity causes burning, swelling, and pain, with a strong pulse and constipation, it’s necessary to clear the bowels with Wuli Dahuang Decoction, or use Leolu and Cimicifuga Decoction, or Lianqiao Xiaodu Powder. If the toxicity is severe but there is external strength and internal weakness, with a weak pulse and fatigue, any signs of deficiency should be addressed. You must support the interior, using Renqi Tori Powder or Tori Xiaodu Powder. If there is Yang deficiency posing as false heat, along with vomiting, nausea, and diarrhea, remedies like Liuwei Huayang Decoction are essential and should not be doubted. If the swelling and pain in the head and neck are severe and intolerable, use Qingliang Jiukushu Powder for external application, or prepare a paste from the juice of natural Platycladus leaves mixed with earthworm mud.[54p]

　　　　　初感治法

　　凡病伤寒瘟疫者，无不发热。然初感之时，其邪在表，未经传里，未至郁热，虽身表有热，不过肤腠之寒邪，而内未有火，岂即阳证？斯时也，但用温散，或兼托散，药对其证，无不即愈。奈何时俗之医，一见发热，便认为火，而芩连知蘗，开手便用，不知内无实热，何以当此？以寒邪得寒药，而表里俱寒，勾连不解则日以内传，寒凉妄用则元阳日败，凡受斯害，死者多矣。此理不明，则既不知表里，又不知先后，终身不省，每至误人，而且敢侈口谈医，其心果亦安乎？[55p]

Initial Concepts of Treatment

In any case of illness, whether due to cold, plague, or fever, there is invariably a rise in temperature. However, at the onset of an illness, when the pathogenic influence is still on the surface and has not penetrated inward or reached the state of congested heat, although there may be a fever at the surface, it is merely due to cold pathogens affecting the skin and layers without the presence of internal fire. How can this be considered a yang condition? At this time, one should only use warming and dispersing methods, perhaps also incorporating mild purging, with the medication tailored to the condition, and it will surely lead to immediate recovery. Yet, unfortunately, the conventional doctors of the time see a fever and immediately assume it to be fire, indiscriminately using herbs like qin, lian, and zhu, not realizing that there is no real heat within. How can such a method be appropriate? If cold pathogens are treated with cold medicines, both the exterior and interior become colder, and if there is no resolution, it will lead to an inward transmission of the cold within days. The reckless use of cold and cooling methods results in the continual decline of the vital yang, causing much loss of life. When this principle is not understood, one becomes oblivious to the conditions of the exterior and interior, as well as the order of treatment. Throughout their lives, they fail to recognize this, often leading others astray, and yet they dare to speak confidently about medicine. Can their hearts truly find peace in such arrogance?[55p]

　　　　　饮食宜忌

　　凡饮食有宜忌者，有不宜忌者。若病伤寒而食不断者，以邪犹在表，未深入也；及其稍深而在半表半里之间，则食渐减矣；再入胸膈胃口，则全不食矣。邪既在胃，则胃口不饥，所以伤寒不食者，或十日或二十日，皆无足虑者，亦以胃气不馁则不败也。但不欲食者，不可强食，强食则助邪。或新愈之后，胃气初醒，尤不可纵食，纵食则食复。此皆大忌也。至有不宜忌者，则如劳倦内伤之人，偶感寒邪，亦必发热，此多以劳伤中气，本非真正伤寒外邪内陷之病，所以外虽发热，而内则饥馁，每多思食。[56p]

Dietary Recommendations and Prohibitions

In matters of diet, there are things that are advisable and things that should be avoided. For those suffering from a cold or fever who cannot stop eating, this indicates that external pathogens are still superficial and have not yet penetrated deeply. As the condition deepens and rests between the superficial and the interior, appetite gradually diminishes. Once the pathogens reach the chest and stomach, one may completely lose the desire to eat. If the pathogen resides in the stomach, one will not feel hungry; thus, in cases of cold, the lack of appetite may last for ten or even twenty days without significant concern, as the stomach’s qi is not depleted. However, if one does not wish to eat, they should not be forced; doing so will support the pathogen. After recovery, when the stomach qi is starting to awaken, it is especially important not to indulge in food, as overindulgence may lead to a relapse. These are all critical prohibitions. As for those who must avoid certain foods, such as individuals with internal injuries due to overwork who happen to catch a cold, they will also likely develop a fever; this is primarily due to damage to the middle qi and not from genuine internal invasion by an external cold pathogen. Therefore, although they may exhibit a fever, they often feel hunger and have a strong desire for food.[56p]

奈何庸昧之辈，但见发热则曰饿不死伤寒，不论虚实，一概禁之。常见欲食者，索之不得，而且加以克伐寒凉之药，嗟嗟！饥肠受剥，虚者益虚，内外夹攻，苦无所诉，及胃气既脱，反不欲食矣。即欲救之，已无可及。予常治此证，每借食为药，所活多人，而见禁食受毙者，亦已不少，故详言之。若病人时时觉饥而索食者，此其邪不在脏，胃中空虚而然，必不可禁，但不宜纵耳。且因此可察虚实，关系非小，不可忽也。　　巢氏曰：凡瘟疫病新瘥，脾胃尚虚，谷气未复，若作劳妄动伤力，并食猪羊鸡犬鱼脍、炙煿肥腻、生果面食硬濇难消之物，停积肠胃，膈闷腹胀便秘，或大吐大下，重复发热，病作不可救矣。
　　　　　避疫法[57p]

How lamentable that the ignorant, upon sensing a fever, declare it to be merely hunger or a cold, without discerning the true nature of the illness, and they indiscriminately impose prohibitions against eating. Those who are hungry often find their requests unmet and are further subjected to harsh medicines that expel cold and dampness. Alas! The hungry bellies suffer, the weak become weaker, and with attacks from both inside and out, they endure suffering without recourse. When the stomach energy has already diminished, they no longer desire food. Even if one wishes to save them, it becomes impossible.

I often treat this condition by using food as medicine, having saved many lives, yet I have also witnessed many perish due to the prohibition of food, so I speak of this matter in detail. If a patient constantly feels hungry and seeks food, it indicates that the pathogen is not within the organs but rather that the stomach is empty; thus, it must not be prohibited, though it should not be indulged excessively. This is crucial for discerning the true condition of the patient and must not be overlooked.

Chao said: In the case of those recovering from an epidemic illness, when the spleen and stomach are still weak and the energy of grains has not yet returned, engaging in excessive activity and consuming fatty meats such as pork, lamb, chicken, fish, as well as hard-to-digest fruits and starchy foods will lead to stagnation in the stomach and intestines, causing bloating and constipation, or severe vomiting and diarrhea, resulting in a recurrence of fever, making the illness incurable.

Avoidance of Epidemic Method.[57p]

　　瘟疫乃天地之邪气，若人身正气内固，则邪不可干，自不相染。故避之之法，惟在节欲节劳。或于房室劳倦之后，尤不可近，仍勿忍饥以受其气，皆要法也。至于却邪之法，则如刺法论所云：天牝从来，复得其往。气出于脑，即不干邪。盖天牝者鼻也，鼻受天之气，故曰天牝。气自空虚而来，亦欲其自空虚而去，即天牝从来，复得其往也。正以气通于鼻，鼻通于脑，毒入脑中，则流布诸经，令人相染矣。气出于脑，谓嚏之，或张鼻以泄之。或受气于室，则泄气于外，而大吸精气以易之，则邪从鼻出而毒气自散，此却邪于外之法也。又如想心如日等法，盖胆属少阳，为中正之官，少阳气壮则脏气赖以俱壮，而邪不能入，此强中御邪之法也。凡探亲诊疾，事有不容已者，但知此诸法，则虽入最秽之地，自可保其无虑。一方治天行时气，宅舍怪异，用降真香烧焚，大解邪秽，小儿带之，能解诸邪，最验。一法，以福建香茶饼不时噙口中，大辟伤寒瘴气秽恶。[58p]

Pestilence is the malevolent energy of heaven and earth. If a person's inner vital energy is strong and upright, then this malevolent force cannot interfere, and one will not be contaminated. Therefore, the method to avoid it lies in moderation in desires and fatigue. Particularly after sexual activity and fatigue, one should keep their distance and avoid enduring hunger to receive its energy; these are essential practices.

As for methods to repel malevolence, as mentioned in the discussion on puncturing, the heavenly energy should continuously return. The energy emanates from the brain, thus not touching the malevolence. The "heavenly energy" refers to the nose, which receives the energy of heaven, hence it is called the heavenly conduit. The energy comes empty and also wishes to leave empty; thus, the heavenly energy continuously returns.

Since energy communicates with the nose, and the nose connects to the brain, if poison enters the brain, it spreads throughout the channels, causing contamination. When energy issues from the brain, one can sneeze or open the nose to release it. If one absorbs energy from a room, then expels it outward while deeply inhaling fresh energy, the malevolent force will escape through the nose, dissipating the toxic energy; this is the method to repel malevolence externally.

Additionally, practices such as visualizing the mind as the sun belong to the Gallbladder, which is affiliated with the Lesser Yang, serving as the central and upright official. When the Lesser Yang energy is strong, the energy of the organs is similarly robust, and thus malevolence cannot enter; this is a method of forcefully resisting malevolence from within.

In all matters of visiting relatives or diagnosing ailments, should circumstances require action, just knowing these methods enables one to remain untroubled even in the dirtiest places. One remedy for dealing with seasonal ailments and strange phenomena in dwellings is to burn Zheng Zhen incense, which greatly dispels malevolence and filth. It is also effective for children to carry it, as it can resolve various evils. A particular method involves sucking on Fujian fragrant tea cakes intermittently to expel the cold and toxic energies.[58p]

　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈士铎】

　　　　　瘟疫治法

　　瘟疫之证，其来无方，然而召之亦有其故。或人事之错乱，或天时之乖违，或尸气之缠染，或毒气之变蒸，皆能成瘟疫之病也。证既不同，治难画一。然而瘟疫之人，大多火热之气，蕴蓄于房户则一家俱病，蕴蓄于村落则一乡俱病，蕴蓄于市廛则一城俱病，蓄畜于道路则千里皆病。故证虽多，但去其火热之气，而少加祛邪逐秽之品，未有不奏功效者也。方用元参五钱，大黄、麦冬、白芍、滑石、花粉各三钱，石膏二钱，柴胡、荆芥各一钱，水煎服。此方可通治瘟疫之病，出入加减，无不奏功。此方之妙，用大黄以荡涤胸腹之邪，用荆芥、柴胡以散其半表半里之邪气，用天花粉以消痰去结，用石膏以逐其胃中之火，用芍药以平肝木，不使来克脾土，则正气自存而邪气自出。此方最妥最神，治瘟疫者，以此为枕中秘。[59p]

Secret Formula of the Stone Chamber: Treatise on Epidemics

The signs of epidemics have no fixed origins, yet there are reasons behind their summoning. It may arise from disturbances in human affairs, deviations in the elemental forces of nature, the contamination from corpses, or the transformation and emission of toxic vapors—all of which can lead to epidemic diseases. Since the manifestations differ, the treatments cannot be unified. However, those afflicted by epidemics mostly harbor a heated energy; when contained within a household, the entire family suffers, when concentrated in a village, the whole community suffers, and when gathered in a marketplace, an entire city suffers; if amassed along roadways, countless distances may fall ill. Thus, while the symptoms vary, addressing the heated energy and minimizing the addition of products meant to expel evils and impurities has proven effective for all.

The formula employs five qian of Yuan Shen, three qian each of Da Huang, Mai Dong, Bai Shao, Hua Fen, two qian of Shi Gao, and one qian each of Chai Hu and Jing Jie, to be boiled in water for consumption. This formula can universally treat epidemic diseases, with adjustments made as needed, all effects are beneficial. The essence of this formula lies in using Da Huang to cleanse the evils from the chest and abdomen, employing Jing Jie and Chai Hu to disperse the mixed external and internal pathogenic energies, employing Tian Hua Fen to eliminate phlegm and resolve blockages, using Shi Gao to eliminate the fire within the stomach, and employing Bai Shao to calm the liver's wood energy, preventing it from overwhelming the spleen's earth energy, thereby sustaining the righteous energy and expelling the evil energy. This formula is the most suitable and miraculous for those treating epidemics, serving as a secret kept close.[59p]

瘟疫门

　　　　方

　　屠苏酒 【《千金方》，下同】 　辟疫气，令人不染温病及伤寒，岁旦屠苏酒方。　　大黄十五铢　白朮　桂心各十八铢　桔梗　蜀椒各五十铢　菝葜十二铢　乌头六铢[六铢：原作「六两」，据《千金》卷九辟温改。]　　右七味(口父)咀，绛袋盛，以十二月晦日日中悬沉井中，令至泥，正月朔日平晓出药，置酒中煎数沸，于东向户中饮之。屠苏之饮，先从小起，多少自在。一人饮，一家无疫。一家饮，一里无疫。饮药酒得三朝，还滓置井中。能仍岁饮，可世无病。当家内外有井，皆悉着药，辟温气也。又一方有防风一两。[60p]

Complete Collection of Medical Works from Ancient and Modern Times, Volume 300

Pestilence Section

Recipe

Tusu Wine: This is a recipe from “Qianjin Prescription.” It dispels pestilential energy, preventing one from contracting warm diseases and typhoid fever. On New Year's Day, make Tusu wine as follows:

  • 15 zhū of rhubarb
  • 18 zhū each of white atractylodes and cassia
  • 50 zhū each of platycodon and Sichuan pepper
  • 12 zhū of peony root
  • 6 zhū of aconite

The above seven ingredients are to be ground and placed in a red bag. On the night of the last day of the twelfth month, suspend this bag in a well until it becomes muddy. On the first day of the first month, retrieve the medicine early in the morning, and decoct it several times in the wine, then drink it in a room facing east.

For Tusu wine, start with a small quantity, adjusting the amount freely. If one person drinks, there will be no pestilence in that household; if an entire household drinks, there will be no pestilence in that neighborhood. If the medicated wine is consumed for three mornings, the dregs should be placed back in the well. If it is drunk again the following year, one can live without illness.

All wells inside and outside the home should be treated with this medicine to dispel pestilential energy. There is also an alternative recipe that includes one liang of siler.[60p]

　　太乙流金散　辟温气。
　　雄黄三两　雌黄　羚羊角烧，各二两　矾石　鬼箭羽各一两半　　右五味，治下筛，三角绛袋盛一两，带心前，并挂门户上。若逢大疫之年，以月旦青布裹一刀圭，中庭烧之。温病人亦烧熏之。
　　雄黄散　辟温气。
　　雄黄五两　朱砂一作赤朮[赤朮：原作「赤木」，据同右改。]　菖蒲　鬼臼各二两　　右四味，治下筛，以涂五心额上鼻人中及耳门。
　　粉身散　辟温病常用。
　　芎藭　白芷　藁本各等分
　　右三味，治下筛，内米粉中以粉身。[61p]

Taiyi Liu Jin San dispels warm qi.
Xiong Huang (realgar) three taels, ci huang (orpiment), antelope horn burnt, each two taels; alum, ghost arrow feathers, each one and a half tael. These five ingredients are ground together, placed in a triangular scarlet pouch weighing one tael, and hung at the door. If encountering a year of great plague, wrap a knife-shaped jade in blue cloth and burn it in the courtyard. Those with warm illnesses should also be burned and smoked.
Xiong Huang San dispels warm qi.
Xiong Huang five taels, zhu sha (cinnabar) one, zhi wu (atractylodes) two, chang pu (calamus), gui jiu (dichroa) each two taels. These four ingredients are ground, and used to anoint the center of the forehead, the space between the nose, and the ear gates.
Fen Shen San is commonly used to dispel warm diseases.
Xiang fu (cyperus), bai zhi (angelica) and gao ben (ligusticum) in equal parts.
These three ingredients are ground together and mixed with rice flour for application.[61p]

　　杀鬼烧药方　辟温气。

　　辟温杀鬼丸　熏百鬼恶气。

Killing Ghosts and Burning Medicinal Recipes to Avert Warmth.

Ingredients:

  • 1 pound each of realgar, cinnabar, and orpiment
  • Antelope horn and goat horn, also permitted
  • Tiger bone, ghost mallow, ghost arrow feathers
  • Wild sage, stone longevity, wild bian, pig feces
  • Horse’s hanging hoof: 3 taels each
  • Qingtang fat, calamus, and white atractylodes: 8 taels each
  • 8 pounds of beeswax

Mix these sixteen ingredients into a fine powder, and knead them with beeswax to form pills the size of pellets. Burn these at dawn, dusk, and in the middle of the night over a small fire in front of the door.

Tiger Head Killing Ghost Pills to Avert Warmth.

  • 5 taels of tiger head
  • 1.5 taels each of cinnabar, realgar, and orpiment
  • 1 tael each of ghost mallow, soap pod, and wild bian

Mix these seven ingredients into a fine powder, and knead them with beeswax to form pills the size of small pellets. Store them in a crimson pouch tied to the arm, left for men and right for women, and hang them in the four corners of the house. On the night of the new moon, burn one pill in the courtyard.

Averting Warmth and Killing Ghost Pills to Exorcise the Evil Spirits of Hundreds of Ghosts.

  • 7 taels each of goat horn and tiger bone
  • 2 taels each of realgar, orpiment, dragon bone, turtle shell, carp shell, and hedgehog skin
  • 15 jujube seeds
  • 5 taels each of ligusticum and pearl
  • 1 chicken head from the eastern gate
  • 1 tael of empty green

Mix these thirteen ingredients into a fine powder and melt 20 taels of wax, then form pills like walnuts. On New Year’s Day, burn one pill in front of the door. Keep one pill with you, tying it to the left for men and right for women to avert all evil. For solitary lodging, mourning, and inquiries about illness, swallow one pill the size of a small bean. On cloudy, foggy days, burn one pill in front of the window, which is auspicious.[62p]

　　雄黄丸　汉建宁[建宁：原作「建炎」，据《千金》卷九辟温改。]二年，太岁在酉，疫气流行，死者极众。即有书生丁季回从蜀青城山来，东过南阳，从西市门入，见患疫疠者颇多，遂于囊中出药，人各惠之一丸。灵药沾唇，疾无不瘥。市中疫鬼数百千余，见书生施药，悉皆惊怖而走。乃有鬼王见书生，谓有道法，兼自施药，感众鬼等奔走若是，遂诣书生，欲求受其道法。　　书生曰：吾无道法，乃囊中之药，呈于鬼王，鬼王睹药，惊惶叩头乞命而走。此方药带之入山，能辟虎狼虫蛇，入水能除水怪蛟蜃。　　雄黄　雌黄　曾青　鬼督邮　珍珠　虎头骨　丹砂　桔梗　白朮　芎藭　白芷　鬼箭羽　芜荑　女青　鬼臼　藜芦　菖蒲　皂荚各一两　　右十八味末之，蜜丸如弹子大，绢袋盛，男左女右带之。卒中恶病及时疫，吞如梧子一丸，烧一弹丸，户内。[63p]

Xiong Huang Pill

In the second year of Han Jian Ning, when the Tai Sui was in the You month, a plague spread, and many people died. A scholar named Ding Jihui came from Qingcheng Mountain in Shu. Upon passing through Nanyang and entering through the west city gate, he saw many afflicted by the plague. He then took out medicine from his pouch and gave each person one pill. The miraculous medicine touched their lips, and there was no illness that did not heal.

In the market, there were hundreds of plague spirits; seeing the scholar administering medicine, they all fled in fear. Then a spirit king approached the scholar and sought to learn his method, moved by the way he dispensed the medicine that made the other spirits flee. The scholar replied: "I have no special method, only the medicine in my pouch." Upon seeing the medicine, the spirit king grew alarmed, bowed his head, and fled for his life.

This medicine, when taken into the mountains, can fend off tigers, wolves, insects, and snakes; when entering water, it can dispel water monsters and creatures like the jiao and shen.

Ingredients:
Realgar, orpiment, Cangqing (A kind of medicinal herb), Gui Duyou (a spirit), pearl, tiger bone, cinnabar, balloon flower root, white atractylodes, ligusticum, white angelica, ghost arrow feather, wild mustard, female Cangqing, ghost saucer, rhizoma of veratrum, sweet flag, and sapindus; each one tael.

Crush these eighteen ingredients into a fine powder, form into pills the size of a marble, store in a silk pouch, with men wearing it on the left and women on the right. If afflicted with a malignant disease or sudden epidemic, swallow one marble-sized pill or burn one pellet at home.[63p]

　　赤散　辟温疫气，伤寒热病。

Liver Warmer Formula

To treat liver organ heat disease, with yin and yang toxins, causing tightness in the nape and back, first cold then heat, tightness in the waist, and brightness in the eyes.

Ingredients:
1 tael of桂心 (cinnamon heart),
3 taels each of白术 (white atractylodes),芒硝 (mirabilite),大青 (large indigo), and栀子 (gardenia),

The above ten ingredients should be chewed, with 9 sheng of water, boiled to extract 3 sheng, divided into three doses.

Another formula for treating liver organ heat disease, with yin and yang toxins, first cold then heat, causing tension in the neck muscles, a red-yellow face, and tightness in the body.

Heart-Warming Formula: To treat warm diseases of the heart and internal organs, with imbalances of yin and yang, toxins, and disturbances. Spleen-Warming Formula: To treat warm diseases of the spleen and internal organs, with imbalances of yin and yang, heaviness in the head and stiff neck, numbness of skin and flesh, and hidden lumps. Ingredients: Da Qing (Isatis), Ling Yang Jiao (Antelope Horn), Sheng Ma (Cimicifuga), She Gan (Belamcanda), Mang Xiao (Natron) each 3 taels; Zhi Zi (Gardenia) 4 taels; Han Shui Shi (Cold Water Stone) 5 taels; Yuan Shen (Ophiopogon) 8 taels. Prepare by grinding the above eight herbs, boil with 7 sheng of water to extract 3 sheng, and divide into three doses.

Lung-Warming Formula: To treat warm diseases of the lung and internal organs, with imbalances of yin and yang, continuous coughing without cessation, and nausea. Ingredients: Xing Ren (Apricot Kernel) and Qian Hu (Peucedanum) each 4 taels; Ma Huang (Ephedra), Zhi Zi (Gardenia), Zi Wan (Aster), Da Qing (Isatis), Yuan Shen (Ophiopogon), Ge Gen (Pueraria) each 3 taels; Gui Xin (Cinnamon Heart) and Gan Cao (Licorice) each 2 taels; Shi Gao (Gypsum) 8 taels. Prepare by grinding the above eleven herbs, boil with 9 sheng of water to extract 3 sheng, and divide into three doses.[66p]

　　肾温方　治肾腑脏温病，身面如刺，腰中欲折，热毒内伤。　　葱白　豉各一升　茵陈　栀子　芒硝各三两　苦参　生葛各四两　生地黄　石膏各八两　　右九味，(口父)咀，以水九升，煮取二升半，下芒硝，分三服。

Shenwen Formula: This treats the warm disease of the kidney organ, with symptoms like prickling sensations on the body surface, a feeling as if the waist is about to break, and internal heat-toxic injury. Ingredients: green onion white (1 sheng), fermented soybeans (1 sheng), garden balsam (3 liang), gardenia fruit (3 liang), mirabilite (3 liang), bitter reed (4 liang), fresh kudzu root (4 liang), fresh rehmannia root (8 liang), gypsum (8 liang). Combine these nine ingredients, chew them, use 9 sheng of water, boil to reduce to 2 and half sheng, add the mirabilite, and divide into three doses.

Weirui Decoction: This treats wind-warm illness, with both yin and yang pulses floating, heavy sweating, and difficulties in breath, leading to numbness and a desire to sleep. For those who have diarrhea, urination becomes difficult; expelling sweat results in incoherent speech, and when acupuncture is applied, patients may suffer from deafness and difficulty in speaking. In this case, it is appropriate to take this remedy. Ingredients: weirui (2 liang), white peony (2 liang), ephedra (2 liang), soleflower (2 liang), apricot kernels (2 liang), chuanxiong (2 liang), licorice (2 liang), qingmu xiang (2 liang), gypsum (3 liang). Combine these nine ingredients, chew, use 8 sheng of water, boil to reduce to 3 sheng, strain, and divide into three doses to induce sweating. If there is a mix of cold and heat, add 1 fen of mirabilite and 3 liang of rhubarb for purging. If there is no wood-scented herb available, replace with 1 fen of musk.

Lou Lu Decoction
Used to treat accumulated heat in internal organs, causing swelling and toxic growths, epidemic lumps, swelling of the head and face, throat blockage, and situations where water medicines cannot be swallowed, in all severe epidemic conditions.

Used for treating fierce epidemic lumps.
Da Huang (Rhubarb), Mu Li (Oyster Shell), and Jiang Can (Silkworm), all in equal parts.
Ground into powder, make honey pills the size of a marble, dissolve each pill in fresh water before taking. Adding Jie Geng and Da Li Zi enhances the efficacy.

Jie Gu Xiong Huang Wan
Prevents epidemic diseases and can be used in the same bed with a patient without transmission through clothing.

No Change in Golden Vitality Powder
Treats seasonal chills and fevers, epidemics and environmental toxins, as well as intermittent chills and fevers, cholera, vomiting, diarrhea, and dysentery (both red and white); it is advisable to take it.

Old Master Divine Vitality Powder
Treats seasonal warm epidemics.
Ingredients:

  • 2 liang of prepared Fu Zi (with peel removed)
  • 2 liang of Bai Zhu
  • 4 liang of prepared Wu Tou (with peel removed)
  • 1 liang of both Jie Geng and Xi Xin
    Preparation: Crush and sift the five ingredients, and store them in a silk bag. If there are no illnesses in the neighborhood, those who do have an epidemic should take a ginger wine dose the size of a thumb, inducing sweating; if they vomit, they will improve. If not relieved after three to four days, take a spoonful with two bowls of water, boil until it bubbles vigorously, and divide into three doses.[70p]

　　务成子萤火丸　主辟瘟疫恶气，百鬼虎狼蛇虺蜂虿诸毒，五兵白刃，盗贼凶害皆辟之。　　萤火　鬼箭削取皮羽　蒺藜各一两　雄黄　雌黄　矾石烧汁尽，各二两　羖羊角　锻灶灰　铁锤柄入铁处烧焦，各一两半　　右九味捣筛为散，以鸡子黄并丹雄鸡冠一具和之，如杏仁大，作三角绢囊盛五丸，带左臂，仍更挂户上。
　　圣散子　苏内翰云：昔尝览《千金》，三建散方，于病无所不治，而孙思邈特为着论，以谓此方用药节度不近人情，至于救急，其验特异。乃知神物效灵，不拘常制，至理开感，智不能知。今予所谓圣散子者，殆此类也。自古论病，惟伤寒为至危急，表里虚实，日数证候，应汗下之类，差之毫厘，辄至不救。若时毒流行，用圣散子者，一切不问阴阳之感，连服取差，不可与伤寒比也。若疾疫之行，平旦辄煮一釜，不问老幼良贱，各一大盏，即时不入其间。平居无病，能空腹一服，则饮食快美，百病不生，济世卫家之宝也。[71p]

The Firefly Pills are meant to ward off pestilence and evil energies, as well as protect against all malevolent spirits, tigers, wolves, snakes, and various poisons, along with weapons and the harm caused by thieves.

To prepare, take one or two of the following: fireflies, the skin and feathers of ghost arrows, and spiny thorns; two drachmas each of realgar, orpiment, and alum, burned until juices are gone; one and a half drachmas of sheep horn; one and a half drachmas of ashes from a forge; and one and a half drachmas of burnt iron hammer handles.

Grind the nine ingredients into powder and mix them with the yolk of a chicken egg and the comb of a male rooster, forming pills the size of almonds. Shape these into three triangular silk pouches containing five pills each, then wear them on the left arm and hang another pouch at the door.

The Holy Powder is discussed by Su Neihan, who mentions a time he examined the “Thousand Gold,” which describes various powdered prescriptions and claims to have no limits in curing diseases. Sun Simiao particularly highlighted that this prescription uses medicinal materials with an unusual balance, effective in emergency situations and producing remarkable results. It shows that miraculous substances work effectively, unrestricted by common methods, and reveal profound truths beyond human understanding. What I refer to as the Holy Powder is akin to this.

Historically, discussions on illness indicate that typhoid fever is the gravest threat; the signs and symptoms vary daily, and if treatment differs by a tiny margin, one may not survive. When poisons are in circulation, using the Holy Powder can address any illness without concern for yin or yang. It should be taken continuously without comparison to typhoid fever. When an outbreak occurs, at dawn, boil a pot, not discerning age or status, and use one large cup for everyone, so that none will be afflicted. If taken on an empty stomach during normal health, it ensures hearty meals and prevents all diseases, serving as a treasure for protecting lives and families.[71p]

其方不知其所从出，而故人巢君世宝之，以治瘟疫，百不失一。余既得之，谪居黄州，连年大疫，所全活者，不可胜数。巢君初甚惜此方，指江水为盟，约不传人，余切隘之，以传蕲水道人庞安常，庞以医闻于世，又善著书，故以授之，且使巢君之名，与此方闻不朽。　　草豆蔻十枚，去皮面裹炮　木猪苓去皮　茯苓　附子炮去皮脐　独活去芦头　石菖蒲　芍药　厚朴去皮姜汁炙　麻黄去根节　槁本去沙土　枳壳去穰麸炒　柴胡去芦头　泽泻　藿香叶　高良姜　华阴细辛　防风去芦头　白朮炒　半夏姜制，各半两　甘草炙，一两　　右銼如麻豆大，每服五钱，水一盏半，煮取八分，去滓热服；余滓两服合为一服，重煎，空心服之。[72p]

The formula is one that is not known for its origin, yet the esteemed physician, Lord Chao, treasured it as a precious remedy for treating epidemics, achieving a remarkable success rate. After acquiring it, I was exiled to Huangzhou, where I faced years of severe outbreaks, during which countless lives were saved. Initially, Lord Chao was very reluctant to share this formula, swearing an oath by the river and agreeing not to pass it on to others. I firmly insisted he divulge it to the Daoist master Pang Anchang of Qishui, as he was renowned for his medical expertise and skill in writing. Thus, it was given to him, ensuring that both Lord Chao's name and the formula would achieve lasting fame.

The ingredients are as follows:

Ten pieces of cardamom, peeled and covered in flour, roasted;
Poria, peeled;
Aconite, roasted and peeled;
Angelica, with the top discarded;
Acorus;
Peony;
Magnolia bark, peeled and ginger-juice roasted;
Ephedra, root and joints removed;
Old stems, free of soil;
Bitter orange peel, fried without the husk;
Bupleurum, top discarded;
Alisma;
Patchouli leaves;
Galanga;
Xixin from Huayin;
Fangfeng, top discarded;
Atractylodes, fried;
Pinellia, processed with ginger, each in equal halves;
Licorice, roasted, one ounce.

The above ingredients should be ground to the size of a mung bean; each dose is five qian, boiled in one and a half cups of water until reduced to eight parts, then strained while hot. The residue can be combined, re-boiled, and taken on an empty stomach.[72p]

Da He Zhong Yin: This is for treating drinks, food stagnation, accumulation, and related symptoms. Use 1 to 2 qian of dried tangerine peel, 1 qian of bitter orange, 5 fen of cardamom, 2 qian each of hawthorn and malt, 1.5 qian each of magnolia bark and poria. Boil with 1.5 sheng of water until reduced to 7 or 8 portions, and take warm after meals.

Bai Shun Wan: This treats all types of Yang pathogenic accumulation, febrile diseases with actual heat, and secretive blockages. Use 1 jin of Sichuan rhubarb (Jinwen variety), and 1.6 qian of stir-fried soapberry (to a light yellow). Grind the above into powder, soak it in water, steam into cakes, and roll into balls about the size of a soy bean. Take 5 fen, or 1 qian, or 2 to 3 qian as appropriate, and wash down with liquid. Honey can also be used for making the pills.

Yi Chai Hu Yin: This treats the invasion of improper seasonal Qi, with cold and heat presenting like malaria. Use 2 to 3 qian of bupleurum, 2 qian of peony, 8 fen of licorice, and 1.5 qian each of scutellaria, raw rehmannia, and dried tangerine peel. Boil with 1.5 sheng of water until reduced to 7 or 8 portions, and take warm.

Er Chai Hu Yin: This treats external pathogens from seasonal changes when there is no internal heat, and should not be recklessly treated with cool medicines. Use 1.5 or 2 to 3 qian of bupleurum, and 1.5 qian each of dried tangerine peel and magnolia bark, 2 qian of pinellia, 1 to 2 qian of asarum, 8 fen of licorice, and add 3 to 5 slices of fresh ginger. Boil with 1.5 sheng of water until reduced to 7 or 8 portions, and take warm.[74p]

Three Chai Hu Decoction: Treats seasonal external pathogens and deficiency of the Yin aspect. Ingredients: Chai Hu 2-3 qian, Shao Yao 1.5 qian, fresh Ginger 3-5 slices, roasted Gan Cao, Chen Pi each 1 qian, Dang Gui 2 qian; for diarrhea, use Shu Di instead. Method: Use 1.5 zhong of water, decoct to 7-8 parts, take warm.

Four Chai Hu Decoction: Treats deficiency of original Qi, and external wind-cold with tight and rapid pulse, the right Qi not prevailing against the evil. Ingredients: Chai Hu 1-3 qian, Ren Shen 2-3 qian or 5-7 qian as needed, roasted Gan Cao 1 qian, fresh Ginger 3-5 slices, Dang Gui 2-3 qian; do not use for those with diarrhea. Method: Use 2 zhong of water, decoct to 7-8 parts, take warm.

Five Chai Hu Decoction: Treats deficiency of the middle Qi, external pathogens not dispersing, simultaneously nourishing blood and Qi to expel cold pathogens. Ingredients: Chai Hu 1-3 qian, Shu Di 3-5 qian, fried Shao Yao 1.5 qian, Dang Gui and Bai Zhu each 2-3 qian, roasted Gan Cao 1 qian, Chen Pi as needed. Method: Use 1.5 zhong of water, decoct to 7 parts, take warm after meals.

Zheng Chai Hu Decoction: Treats the initial stage of external infection with balanced blood and Qi. Ingredients: Chai Hu 1-3 qian, Shao Yao 2 qian, Chen Pi 1.5 qian, Fang Feng and Gan Cao each 1 qian, fresh Ginger 3-5 slices. Method: Use 1.5 zhong of water, decoct to 7-8 parts, take hot.[75p]

　　麻桂饮　治瘟疫阴寒气胜，夏月不必厚盖，津津透彻为度。　　官桂一二钱　当归三四钱　陈皮随宜或不用　麻黄二三钱　炙甘草一钱　　水一锺半，加姜五七片或十片，煎八分，去浮沫，不拘时服。

Mao Gui Drink: Treats pestilence caused by excess cold and yin energy. During summer months, thick blankets are unnecessary; moderation is key.
Ingredients: 1-2 qian of Guo Gui, 3-4 qian of Dang Gui, Chen Pi as needed or omitted, 2-3 qian of Ma Huang, 1 qian of roasted Gan Cao. Use 1.5 sheng of water, add 5-10 slices of ginger, boil down to 8 parts, skim off the foam, and take as needed.

Da Wen Zhong Drink: Treats cold pestilence from all seasons, marked by extreme deficiency of original yang, where upright energy cannot overcome pathogenic factors.
Ingredients: 3-5-7 qian of Shou Di, 3-5 qian each of Bai Zhu and Dang Gui (substitute Shan Yao for diarrhea), 2-3 qian of Ren Shen (up to 1 liang in severe cases, or omitted), 1 qian of roasted Gan Cao, 2-3-4 qian of Chai Hu, 1-2-3 qian of Ma Huang, 1-2 qian of Rou Gui, 1-2 qian of dry ginger (or 3-5-7 slices of fresh ginger). Use 2 sheng of water, boil down to 7 parts, skim off the foam, and drink warm, possibly lightly covered to induce slight sweating.

Chai Chen Decoction: Treats cough with excessive phlegm from exterior invasion.
Ingredients: 2-3 qian of Chai Hu, 1.5 qian of Chen Pi, 3-5-7 slices of fresh ginger, 2 qian each of Ban Xia and Fu Ling, 1 qian of Gan Cao. Use 1.5 sheng of water, boil down to 7 parts, and take warm away from meals.

Chai Qin Decoction: Treats unresolved exterior pathogen with internal and external heat, marked by a slippery and rapid pulse.
Ingredients: 2-3 qian of Chai Hu, 1.5 qian of Zhi Qiao, 2 qian each of Huang Qin, Zhi Zi, Ze Xie, and Mu Tong. Use 2 sheng of water, boil down to 7 parts, and take warm.[76p]

Gui Ge Drink: For treating symptoms of Yangming during hot and humid seasons, with heat-induced thirst and dryness of fluids, where yin is deficient and sweat cannot be produced. Ingredients: 3-5 qian of Dong Gui, 2-3 qian of Gan Ge. Use 2 zhong of water, decoct to 1 zhong, cool it in cold water, and drink gradually. When sweating occurs, the condition is resolved.

Gui Chai Drink: For treating external conditions affecting the nutritive qi, where sweating cannot occur; a divine formula. Ingredients: 1 liang of Dong Gui, 5 qian of Chai Hu, 8 fen of roasted Gan Cao. Use 1.5 zhong of water and decoct.

Tai Qing Drink: For treating stomach heat causing restlessness and vomiting. Ingredients: 1.5 qian each of Zhi Mu, Shi Hu, and Mu Tong, 5-7 qian of Sheng Shi Gao. Use 1.5 zhong of water, decoct to 7 parts, and take warm or cool. Can also add Mai Men Dong.

Yu Nu Decoction: For treating water deficiency and excess heat, with pulse being floating, surging, and large. Ingredients: 3-5 qian of Sheng Shi Gao, 3-5 qian or 1 liang of Shu Di, 0.5 qian each of Zhi Mu and Niu Xi, 2 qian of Mai Dong. Use 1.5 zhong of water, decoct to 7 parts, and take warm or cool.

Yu Quan Powder: Also known as Sweet Dew Powder. For treating internal heat of Yangming, warm epidemic spots, and yellowing. Ingredients: 6 liang of Sheng Shi Gao, 1 liang of powdered Gan Cao. Grind to a very fine powder. Each dose is 1-3 qian, mixed with freshly drawn water, hot soup, or ginseng soup. Adding 3 qian of Zhu Sha also enhances its effectiveness.[77p]

　　雪梨浆　解烦热，退阴火，生津止渴。　　清香甘美大梨削去皮
　　别用大碗盛清冷甘泉，将梨薄切浸于水中，少顷，水必甘美，但频饮其水，勿食其滓。退阴火极速也。
　　六味回阳饮　治阴阳将脱等证。

　　理阴煎　治真阴不足，忽感寒邪，服此不攻自散。　　熟地三五七钱或一二两　炙甘草一二钱　当归二三钱或五七钱　干姜炒黄色，一二三钱　或加肉桂一二钱　　水二锺，煎七八分，热服。

　　温胃饮　治寒疫呕吐泄泻。

Snow Pear Syrup: Relieves heat, dispels yin fire, produces fluids, and quells thirst.

Take a large, sweet pear and peel it. Use a large bowl to hold cool, sweet spring water, slice the pear thinly, and soak it in the water. After a while, the water will become sweet; drink the water frequently but do not eat the dregs. This quickly dispels yin fire.

Six-Flavor Returning Yang Decoction: Treats symptoms of yin and yang separation.
Ingredients: 1-2 taels of ginseng or a few qian, 1 qian of roasted licorice, processed aconite, and roasted dried ginger each 2-3 qian, and 3 qian of angelica; for diarrhea or bleeding, replace with winter worm. Use 5 qian or 1 tael of cooked rehmannia. Add 2 bowls of water, decoct with strong heat until 7-8 parts remain, and take warm.

Yin Regulating Decoction: Treats deficiency of true yin, sudden cold invasion, takes effect without needing aggressive treatment.
Ingredients: 3-5-7 qian or 1-2 taels of cooked rehmannia, 1-2 qian of roasted licorice, 2-3 qian or 5-7 qian of angelica, roasted dried ginger (yellow), 1-2-3 qian, optionally add cinnamon 1-2 qian. Use 2 bowls of water, decoct until 7-8 parts remain, take warm.

Warm Stomach Drink: Treats cold epidemic, vomiting, and diarrhea.
Ingredients: 1-2-3 qian or 1 tael of ginseng, 1-2 qian or 1 tael of roasted white atractylodes, 1-2 qian of angelica (do not use for diarrhea), 2 qian of roasted hyacinth bean, 1 qian each of roasted licorice and dried tangerine peel (optional), 1-2-3 qian of roasted dried ginger until charred. Use 2 bowls of water, decoct until 7 parts remain, take warm away from meals.[78p]

　　柴葛煎　治瘟疫表里俱热。
　　柴胡　干葛　黄芩　连翘　芍药　甘草　　水一锺半，煎服。

　　　　单方

　　天气不和，疫病流行：预备一物柏枝散，取南向社中柏东南枝，曝令干，捣末酒服方寸匕，神良。　　【《千金方》，下同】
　　又方：正月旦取东行桑根如指长七寸，以丹涂之，悬门户上，又令人带之。
　　断温病不相染着方：汲水瓶一，长七寸，盗着病人卧席下，良。　　又方：以绳度所住户中壁，屈绳即断之。[79p]

Five Noble Herbs Decoction: Treats spleen and stomach deficiency due to cold and dampness.
Ingredients: 2-3 qian of ginseng, 2 qian each of white atractylodes and poria, 1 qian of licorice, and 1-2 qian of dry ginger (fried until yellow). Water: 1.5 sheng. Decoction for consumption.

Stomach Connection Decoction: Treats symptoms of spleen and kidney deficiency due to cold.
Ingredients: 3-5 qian or 1 liang of cooked rehmannia, 1-2 qian of honey-fried licorice, 2 qian each of fried yam and fried white hyacinth bean, 0.5-0.7 qian of processed evodia, 1-3 qian each of charred dry ginger and fried white atractylodes. Water: 2 sheng, decoct for 7 minutes, take warm away from meals.

Chai Ge Decoction: Treats both exterior and interior heat due to plague.
Ingredients: Water: 1.5 sheng, decoct with chihuo (bupleurum), dry kudzu, scutellaria, forsythia, peony, licorice.

Single Prescription:
When the weather is unbalanced and epidemics are prevalent: prepare a variety of cypress branch powder, taking southeast branches of cypress facing south, sun-dry, pound into powder, take with wine size of a thumb, it is effective.
Another method: on the first day of the first month, take a mulberry root as long as seven inches, paint it with red and hang it at the entrance.
To prevent warmth disease from spreading: use a water bottle of seven inches, place it under the patient's sleeping area, it is effective.
Another method: measure the wall of the household with a string, and cut the string where it bends.[79p]

　　治温病不相染方：以桃树蠹屎末之，水服方寸匕。　　又方：朮、豉等分，酒渍服之，妙。　　又方：正旦吞麻子、赤小豆各二十七粒，又以二七粒投井中。　　又方：新布袋盛赤豆一升，内井中三日出，举家服二十七枚。　　又方：松叶末之，酒服方寸匕，日三服。　　又方：常以七月七日，合家吞赤小豆，向日吞二七枚。　　又方：常以七月七日，男吞大豆七枚，女吞小豆二七枚。　　又方：神仙教人立春后有庚子日，温芜菁葅汁，合家大小并服，不限多少　　治温令不相染：新布袋盛大豆一升，内井中一宿出，服七枚。
　　温疫：用白药子二枚为末，水服之。　　又方：白蜜和上色朱砂粉一两，以太岁日平旦大小勿食，向东方立，吞服三七丸，如麻子大，勿令齿近之；并吞赤小豆七枚，投井泉中。终身勿忘此法。　　又方：凡时行疫疠，常以月望日，细銼东引桃枝，煮汤浴之。[80p]

Treatment for warm diseases without mutual infection: Use powdered excrement of peach tree pests, taken with a mouthful of water. Another method: Mix equal parts of atractylodes and fermented soybeans, soaked in wine and taken. Another method: On the New Year, swallow twenty-seven seeds of hemp and red beans, and throw another twenty-seven into a well. Another method: Place one liter of red beans in a new cloth bag, put it in a well for three days, and the whole family takes twenty-seven pieces. Another method: Powder pine needles and take a mouthful with wine three times a day. Another method: On July 7, the whole family should swallow red beans, taking twenty-seven pieces facing the sun. Another method: On July 7, males take seven large beans, and females take twenty-seven small beans. Another method: Celestial beings teach that after the beginning of spring, on the day of Gengzi, juice from warm turnips is to be consumed by everyone, regardless of quantity.

To prevent infection from warmth: Place one liter of large beans in a new cloth bag, leave it in a well overnight, and take seven pieces.

For warm epidemics: Use two pieces of white medicine as powder, and take with water. Another method: Mix one tael of white honey with powdered red cinnabar, and on the day of the Tai Sui at dawn, do not eat anything, stand facing the east, and swallow three seven-sized pills, about the size of a hemp seed, avoiding contact with the teeth; also swallow seven red beans and throw them into a well. This method must not be forgotten for a lifetime. Another method: During epidemics, regularly on the full moon day, finely shave peach branches from the east, boil them, and bathe in the broth.[80p]

　　瘴疠气方：蒜五子并皮碎之，豉心一升，二味以三岁男儿尿二升，煮五六沸，去滓服之，良。　　又方：青竹茹二升，以水四升，煮取三升，分作三服。
　　治患雾气者，心内烦闷少气，头痛项急，起则眼眩欲倒，身微热，战掉不安，时复憎寒，心中欲吐，吐时无物：方用新猪屎二升半，内好酒一升，搅令散，以生布绞取汁，更以绵滤，顿服之，取尽，即地铺暖卧覆盖，铺前着火，当汗出。若得汗，当细细去上衣，勿使心寒，寒即不差。看汗自干乃起，慎风冷。
　　辟禳时疫：半天河水饮之。 【《医林集要》】
　　时气欲死：大钱百文，水一斗，煮八升，入麝香末三分，稍饮至尽，或吐，或下愈。 【《肘后方》，下同。】
　　时气温病，头痛壮热，脉大，始得一日者：比轮钱一百五十七文，水一斗，煮取七升，服汁，须臾，复以水五升，更煮一升，以水二升，投中，合得三升，出钱饮汁，当吐毒出也。[81p]

Prescribing for epidemic miasma: Crush five cloves of garlic with their skins, and one sheng of fermented soybeans; blend these two ingredients with two sheng of the urine from a three-year-old boy, boil until five or six bubbles form, remove the dregs and consume the liquid—it is effective.

Another formula: Take two sheng of green bamboo leaves, add four sheng of water, boil down to three sheng, and divide into three doses.

To treat ailments from foggy air, symptoms include internal restlessness, shortness of breath, headache, and tightness in the neck. When standing, dizziness occurs, body slightly warm, experiencing chills and discomfort, feeling nauseous without vomit: use two and a half sheng of fresh pig manure, one sheng of good wine, stir until it dissolves, then strain with a fine cloth to extract the juice, and follow up with cotton filtering; consume it all at once. Then lie down on a warm surface covered up, placing a fire in front to induce sweating. Once sweating begins, while ensuring not to expose the heart to cold, carefully remove the top garment, as cold will induce further problems. Wait until the sweat dries completely before getting up, being cautious of wind and cold.

To ward off and alleviate epidemic diseases: Drink water from the Half River.

For acute seasonal sickness: One hundred large coins, one dou of water, boil to eight sheng, add three fen of musk powder, sip until finished; if vomit or diarrhea occurs, it will lead to recovery.

For warm seasonal diseases with headaches, high fever, and strong pulse, for instances occurring for the first day: Use one hundred and fifty-seven coins, one dou of water, boil down to seven sheng, consume the juice, shortly after, boil another liter of water in five sheng, mix together to yield three sheng, and consume the juice to expel the poison.[81p]

　　温病热甚，饮水成暴冷啘者：茅根切，枇杷叶拭去毛，炙香各半斤，水四升，煎二升，去滓，稍稍饮之。【庞安常《伤寒卒病论》，下同】
　　温病伏热在胃，令人胸满则气逆，逆则哕或大下，胃中虚冷亦致哕也。茅根切，葛根切，各半斤，水三升，煎一升半，每温饮一(角戋)，气止即停。
　　伤寒时气温疫，头痛壮热脉盛：以干艾叶三升，水一斗，煮一升，顿服取汗。 【《肘后方》】
　　疫病不染：五月五日午时，多釆苍耳嫩叶，阴干收之，临时为末，冷水服二钱，或水煎，举家皆服，能辟邪恶。【《千金方》】
　　天行热狂：芭蕉根捣汁饮之。 【《日华》】
　　时气余热不退，烦躁发渴，四肢无力，不能饮食：用牛蒡根捣汁，服一小盏效。 【《圣惠方》】
　　天行时疾：生牛蒡根捣汁五合，空腹分为二服服讫，取桑叶一把炙黄，以水一升，煮取五合，顿服取汗。无叶用枝。【《千金方》】[82p]

For high fever due to warm disease, if drinking water causes violent coldness: Cut the roots of miscanthus and wipe the leaf of loquat to remove the fuzz, each half a pound, add four liters of water, decoct to two liters, strain, and drink slowly.

For warm disease with heat lurking in the stomach, causing fullness in the chest and counterflow of qi which may lead to belching or severe diarrhea, or if the stomach is cold and empty, causing belching: Cut roots of miscanthus and kudzu, each half a pound, with three liters of water, decoct to one and a half liters, and drink warm in small amounts, stopping once the qi settles.

For cold damage during the warm epidemic season, with headache, strong fever, and full pulse: Use three liters of dried mugwort leaves, one dou of water, boil to one liter, and take in a single dose to induce sweating.

To avoid infection from epidemic diseases: On the fifth day of the fifth month, around noon, gather tender leaves of cyanthus, dry them in the shade, powder them for use, take two qian with cold water, or decoct them, for the entire family to consume, which can repel evil.

For rampant heat from warm pathogen: Crush banana plant roots and drink the juice.

When residual heat from seasonal pathogens does not dissipate, causing irritability and thirst, and weakness in limbs, unable to eat or drink: Use burdock root, crush to extract juice, and take a small cup.

For seasonal diseases: Take five he of fresh burdock root, divide into two doses when fasting, and after taking it, prepare a handful of mulberry leaves, roast until yellow, boil with one liter of water to obtain five he, and take in a single dose to induce sweating. If there are no leaves, use the branches.[82p]

　　天行热病，初起一二日者：麻黄一大两，去节，以水四升，煮去沫，取二升，去滓，着米一匙及豉，为稀粥，先以汤浴后，乃食粥，厚覆取汗，即愈。【《必用方》】
　　温毒发斑呕逆：名黑膏。生地黄二两六钱二字半，好豆豉一两六钱二字半，以猪膏十两合之，露一夜，煎减三分之一，绞去滓，入雄黄、麝香如豆大，搅匀分作三服，毒从皮中出则愈。忌芜荑。【《千金方》】
　　辟禳瘟疫：正月上寅日，捣女青末，三角绛囊盛，系帐中，大吉。 【《肘后方》，下同】
　　时疫流毒攻手足，肿痛欲断：用虎杖根銼煮汁渍之，良。
　　天行毒病，七八日热积胞中，烦乱欲死：凝雪汤。用芫花一斤，水三升，煮取一升半，渍故布，薄胸上，不过再三薄，热则除，当温四肢，护厥逆也。【《千金方》】
　　时疾发黄，狂闷烦热不识人者：大(艹舌)蒌实黄者一枚，以新汲水九合，浸淘取汁，入蜜半合，(石卜)硝八分，尽分再服，便瘥。【《图经》】[83p]

  1. For the onset of a febrile illness in the heavens during the first day or two: take one large dose of ephedra (Ma Huang), removing the nodes, with four liters of water, boil to remove foam, take two liters, strain out the residue, add a spoonful of rice and fermented soybeans to make a thin porridge. First bathe with the broth, then eat the porridge, cover warmly to induce sweating, and this will cure you.

  2. For symptoms of warm toxin manifesting as spots, with vomiting and reversal: known as black ointment. Use two and a half taels of raw Rehmannia, one and a half taels of good fermented soybeans, and mix with ten taels of pig fat. Let it sit overnight, then boil down by one third, strain out the residue, add realgar and musk in bean-sized portions, mix thoroughly and divide into three doses. When the poison exits through the skin, you will be cured. Avoid using wild coltsfoot.

  3. To dispel and ward off epidemics: on the first day of the first month, pound the powder of female blue herb, place it in a triangular red bag, and hang it in the tent for great luck.

  4. For epidemics causing toxins to attack the hands and feet, resulting in swelling and pain: use the root of Japanese knotweed, ground and boiled to make a juice for soaking.

  5. For febrile illness lasting seven or eight days, with heat accumulating in the body, causing agitation and a desire to die: use snow-congealed soup. Take one pound of siler and three liters of water, boil down to one and a half liters, soak a piece of old cloth, apply thinly to the chest, not more than three layers; if heated, it will be removed. Warm the limbs to protect against reversal.

  6. For sudden jaundice with mad delirium and fever, unable to recognize people: take one ripe fruit of large (Atractylodes) and soak it in nine qian of newly drawn water, then extract the juice. Add half a cup of honey and eight parts of saltpeter, mix and take until finished, which will bring healing.[83p]

　　时气头痛壮热：生葛根洗净捣汁一大盏，豉一合，煎六分，去滓服，汗出即瘥。未汗再服。若心热，加栀子仁十枚。【《圣惠方》】
　　钓樟置门上，辟天行时气。 【萧炳】
　　天行余毒，手足肿痛欲断：作坑深三尺，烧煎灌酒，着屐居坑上，以衣壅之，勿令泄气。【《类要》】
　　时疾头痛发热者：以连根葱白二十根，和米煮粥，入酢少许，热食取汗，即解。 【《济生秘览》】
　　时气温病，初得头痛壮热脉大：即以小蒜一升，杵汁三合顿服，不过再作，便愈。 【《肘后方》】
　　禳解疫气：六月六日釆马齿苋晒干，元旦煮熟，同盐酢食之，可解疫疠气。 【经验方】
　　温病食劳：杏仁五两，酢二升，煎取一升服之，取汗瘥。 【《类要》】
　　预辟瘴疠：桃仁一斤，吴茱萸、青盐各四两同炒熟，以新瓶密封一七，取出，拣去茱盐，将桃仁去皮尖，每嚼一二十枚，山居尤宜之。【《选奇方》】[84p]

  • For a fever with a headache: Wash and crush fresh kudzu root to extract a large cup of juice, mix with a measure of fermented soybeans, boil down to about six parts, strain and take; sweating will relieve the condition. If sweating does not occur, take again. If there is heart heat, add ten peach kernels.

  • Place camphor wood above the door to ward off seasonal diseases.

  • If there is residual toxicity from seasonal diseases causing swelling and pain in the hands and feet: Dig a pit three feet deep, boil and soak in wine, stand in the pit wearing wooden clogs, and cover with clothing to prevent the escape of vapors.

  • For headaches and fever due to seasonal diseases: Use twenty roots of green onion, cook them with rice to make porridge, add a little vinegar, eat hot to induce sweating, which will relieve the condition.

  • For warm diseases presenting with headache, fever, and a strong pulse: Take one liter of minced garlic and ingest it all at once, with no need for further doses, and you will recover.

  • To dispel epidemic qi: On the sixth day of the sixth month, gather and dry purslane, then cook it on New Year's Day, combining it with salt and vinegar to eat; it can dispel epidemic pestilence.

  • For warm diseases from overexertion: Take five taels of apricot kernels and two liters of vinegar, boil down to one liter to drink, inducing sweating to relieve symptoms.

  • To prevent pestilence: Take one pound of peach kernels, and four taels each of evodia fruit and green salt, fry until cooked, seal them in a new bottle for seven days, take out, remove the salt and evodia, peel the peach kernels, and chew twenty or so each time, especially beneficial for those living in mountainous areas.[84p]

　　伤寒温疫已发未发：用梨木皮、大甘草各一两，黄秫谷一合为末，锅底煤一钱，每服三钱，白汤下。日二服取愈。【《简易方》】
　　温病发哕，因饮水多者：枇杷叶去毛炙香，茅根各半斤，水四升，煎二升，稍稍饮之。【庞安常方】
　　时气烦渴：生藕汁一盏，生蜜一合，和匀细服。 【《圣惠方》】
　　天行温疫：松叶细切，酒服方寸匕，日三服，能辟五年瘟。 【《伤寒类要》】
　　辟禳瘟疫：每腊月二十四日五更，取第一汲井水，浸乳香，至元旦五更温热，从小至大，每人以乳一块，饮水三呷，则一年无时灾。孔平仲云：此乃宣圣之方，孔氏七十余代用之也。
　　时气温病，头痛壮热，初得一日：用生梓木削去黑皮，取里白者切一升，水二升五合煎汁，每服八合，取瘥。【《肘后方》，下同】
　　时行发黄：竹叶五升切，小麦七升，石膏三两，水一斗半，煮取七升，细服，尽剂愈。[85p]

  • For injuries from cold or warm epidemics that have or have not occurred: use one ounce each of pear tree bark and licorice, along with a handful of yellow millet ground into powder, and one penny of stove coal. Take three pennies of this mixture with warm water twice daily until recovery.

  • For warm diseases causing cough, especially due to excessive water intake: use half a pound each of loquat leaves (after removing hairs) and reeds, boil with four liters of water until two liters remain, and drink gradually.

  • For seasonal thirst: mix a cup of fresh lotus root juice with a handful of raw honey, stir well and take small sips.

  • For ailments caused by seasonal warm epidemics: finely chop pine needles and take a small spoonful with wine three times a day; this can ward off epidemics for five years.

  • To ward off and mitigate epidemics: on the morning of the 24th day of the twelfth month, collect the first drawn well water and soak frankincense in it. By the fifth day of the New Year, warm it up, and each person should drink three sips, with a piece of frankincense. This practice will prevent disasters for the entire year. Confucius Pingzhong states that this method has been passed down for over seventy generations in the Confucian family.

  • For seasonal warm diseases with fever and headache, occurring on the first day of onset: peel off the black skin of fresh catalpa wood, take one liter of the white inner part, and boil it with two and a half liters of water to extract the juice, taking eight ounces at each dose until recovery.

  • For seasonal jaundice: cut five liters of bamboo leaves, seven liters of wheat, and three ounces of gypsum, boil with one and a half buckets of water until seven liters remain, and take in small doses until cured.[85p]

　　风热邪病：虾蟆烧灰、朱砂等分为末，每服一钱，酒服，日三甚有神验。 【《外台秘要》】
　　热病下痢欲死者：龙骨半斤研，水一升，煮取五合，候极冷稍饮，得汗取愈，效。 【《肘后方》】
　　热病目暗，因差后食五辛而致：用鲫鱼作臛食之。 【《集验方》】
　　预辟温疫：鲍鱼头烧灰方寸匕，合小豆末七枚，米饮服之，令瘟疫气不相染也。 【《肘后方》，下同】
　　辟禳瘟疫：冬至日取赤雄鸡作腊，至立春日煮食至尽，勿分他人。
　　时行发黄：用金色脚黄雌鸡，治如食法，煮熟食之，并饮汁令尽，不过再作。亦可少下盐豉。
　　天行不解，已汗者：用新生鸡子五枚，倾盏中，入水一鸡子搅浑，以水一升煮沸投入，纳少酱啜之，令汗出愈。【许仁则方】
　　天行呕逆，食入即吐：鸡子一枚，水煮三五沸，冷水浸少顷吞之。 【《外台》】
　　时行发黄：酢酒浸鸡子一宿，吞其白数枚。 【《肘后方》，下同】[86p]

  1. For diseases caused by wind-heat: Grind to a powder to equal parts of toad ash and cinnabar. Take one penny with wine three times a day for significant efficacy.

  2. For severe heat illness with diarrhea: Grind half a pound of dragon bone, boil it in one liter of water to extract five cups. Wait until it cools slightly, then drink. Sweating will lead to recovery.

  3. For heat illness with darkened vision from excessive consumption of five pungent foods: Use carp to make a dish for consumption.

  4. To prevent warm epidemics: Burn the head of abalone to ash, mix with seven portions of adzuki bean powder, and take with rice wine to ward off epidemic influences.

  5. To avert and remedy epidemics: On the Winter Solstice, take a red rooster and prepare it as preserved meat. By the Spring Equinox, cook it until fully consumed without sharing with others.

  6. For seasonal yellowing: Use a golden-footed yellow hen, treat as per the previous method, cook until done, and eat it along with the juice. Do not prepare more than once. A little salt and fermented soy might also be added.

  7. For persistent symptoms with sweating: Use five fresh eggs, place them in a cup, add water and stir, then immerse them in one liter of boiling water. Add a little soy sauce and consume to induce sweating for recovery.

  8. For seasonal sickness with vomiting: Take one egg, boil it in water for three to five times, then soak it in cold water for a while before swallowing.

  9. For seasonal yellowing: Soak eggs in vinegar wine overnight and swallow several of the whites.[86p]

　　伤寒时气：猪膏如弹丸，温水化服，日三次。
　　天行劳复：合头垢枣核大，服一枚良。 【《类要》】
　　热病发狂，奔走似癫，如见鬼神，久不得汗，及不知人事者：以人中黄入大罐内，以泥固济煅半日，去火毒研末，新汲水服三钱。未退再服。【《斗门方》】
　　大头天行：羌活、酒黄芩、酒蒸大黄，水煎服。 【东垣】　　又方：歌曰：人间治疫有仙方，一两僵蚕二大黄，姜汁为丸如弹子，井华调蜜便清凉。【丹溪】
　　瘟疫热病，上焦邪实，或痰食气逆不通：用萝卜子捣碎，温汤和搅，取淡汤徐徐饮之，少顷当吐。有吐不尽者，必从下行。或为末，温水调服一匙，亦妙。【《景岳全书》，下同】　　又方：用盐少许，于锅中炒红色，入水煮，至将滚未滚之际搅匀，试其滋味稍淡，每饮半碗，渐次增饮，自吐。以病去为度。　　又方：诸药皆可取吐，但随证作汤剂探吐之。[87p]

During a time of cold damage: Pig fat like a ball, dissolve in warm water and take three times a day.

For ailments caused by climatic stress: A piece the size of a jujube pit, take one.

For fever-induced madness, running around like a madman, seeing ghosts, not sweating for a long time, and not knowing people or situations: Take human bile and place it in a large jar, mix with clay and bake for half a day to remove the fire toxins, grind into powder, and take three qians with freshly drawn water. If symptoms persist, take again.

For great head fevers: Use Qianghuo, yellow gentian, and large yellow (rhubarb) steamed with wine, then decoct in water to take.

Another formulation: There is a miraculous remedy for treating epidemics: one tael of dried silkworms and two large yellow (rhubarbs), mix with ginger juice into balls like pellets, and adjust with well water and honey for a refreshing effect.

For pestilential heat diseases with upper jiao (upper organ) obstruction or phlegm with food causing reversed qi: Crush radish seeds, mix with warm soup, and drink the diluted liquid slowly until you feel an urge to vomit. If vomiting is incomplete, it will be expelled from below. Alternatively, grind to powder and take with warm water, one spoonful, which is also effective.

Another formulation: Use a small amount of salt and roast until red in a pan, then add water, stirring until just before boiling, and test the taste until it is slightly bland, drink half a bowl at a time, gradually increasing the amount until vomiting occurs. Use the cessation of illness as a measure.

Another formulation: Various medicines can induce vomiting, but should be prepared as a decoction according to the symptoms to facilitate vomiting.[87p]

　　天行瘟疫：取初病人衣，于甑上蒸过，则一家不染。 【时珍】　　又方：桃蠹虫粪为末，水服方寸匕，令不相染。 【《子母秘录》】　　又方：五月一日取土或砖石，入瓦器中，埋着门外阶下，合家不患时气。 【藏器，下同】　　又方：正旦取古冢砖，咒悬大门上，一年无疫疾。
　　　　导引

　　《素问》刺法论入疫室辟传染法。帝曰：余闻五疫之至，皆相染易，无问大小，病状相似，不施救疗，如何可得不相移易者？岐伯曰：不相染者，正气存内，邪不可干，避其毒气。天牝从来，复得其往。气出于脑，即不干邗。气出于脑，即先想心如日。欲将入于疫室，先想青气自肝而出，左行于东，化作林木；次想白气自肺而出，右行于西，化作戈甲；次想赤气自心而出，南行于上，化作焰明；次想黑气自肾而出，北行于下，化作水；次想黄气自脾而出，存于中央，化作土。五气护身之毕，以想头上，如北斗之煌煌，然后可入于疫室。
[88p]

The celestial movement of epidemics: Take the clothing of an initial patient, steam it over a pot, and then the entire family will remain uninfected.

Another method: Use powdered excrement from peach borer insects, take a spoonful with water, and it will prevent contagion.

Another method: On the first day of May, take soil or bricks and stones, place them in a pottery vessel, bury them outside the doorsteps, and the entire household will not suffer from seasonal ailments.

Another method: On New Year’s Day, take bricks from ancient tombs, chant incantations, and hang them above the main door, ensuring a year without epidemics.

Guidance

In the "Suwen," the discussion on acupuncture methods addresses the prevention of transmission in an epidemic chamber. The Emperor said: I have heard that when five epidemics arrive, they easily transmit among each other, regardless of severity, and the symptoms are similar; if no treatment is applied, how can one avoid contagion? Qibo replied: To avoid contagion, one must preserve the righteous qi within, so that evil cannot invade, thus avoiding its toxic influence. The celestial essence has always existed and can return to its original state.

The qi emanates from the brain, preventing interference. When the qi flows from the brain, first focus your thoughts as if the heart were like the sun. When entering an epidemic chamber, first visualize the blue qi emanating from the liver, moving left towards the east, transforming into trees; next, visualize the white qi from the lungs, moving right towards the west, transforming into weaponry; then, visualize the red qi from the heart, moving south above, transforming into flames; next, visualize the black qi from the kidneys, moving north below, transforming into water; finally, visualize the yellow qi from the spleen, residing in the center, transforming into earth. By completing the protection of the five qís, visualize them above your head, like the brilliance of the Big Dipper, then one may enter the epidemic chamber.[88p]
